By [date] in order to contribute to the consistent application of geographical surveys and forecasts, BEREC shall, after consulting stakeholders and in close cooperation with the Commission, issue guidelines to assist national regulatory authorities on the consistent implementation of their obligations under this Article.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.6 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a0623\n\n\nConsultation and transparency mechanism\n\n\nExcept in cases falling within Articles\u00a0732(9), 2026, or\u00a021\u00a027, Member States shall ensure that, where national regulatory authorities \u00d6\u00a0or other competent authorities\u00a0\u00d5 intend to take measures in accordance with this Directive or the Specific Directives, or where they intend to provide for restrictions in accordance with Article\u00a09(3)45(4) and\u00a09(4)45(5), which have a significant impact on the relevant market, they give interested parties the opportunity to comment on the draft measure within a reasonable period \u00f0\u00a0, having regard to the complexity of the matter and in any event not shorter than 30 days, except in exceptional circumstances\u00a0\u00ef.\n\n\nNational regulatory \u00d6\u00a0and other competent\u00a0\u00d5 authorities shall publish their national consultation procedures.\n\n\nMember States shall ensure the establishment of a single information point through which all current consultations can be accessed.\n\n\nThe results of the consultation procedure shall be made publicly available by the national regulatory authority, except in the case of confidential information in accordance with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 and national law on business confidentiality.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\n\nArticle\u00a03324\n\n\nConsultation with interested parties\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.23(a)\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure as far as appropriate that national regulatory authorities take account of the views of end-users, consumers (including, in particular, disabled consumers), manufacturers and undertakings that provide electronic communications networks and/or services on issues related to all end-user and consumer rights concerning publicly available electronic communications services, in particular where they have a significant impact on the market.\n\n\nIn particular, Member States shall ensure that national regulatory authorities establish a consultation mechanism ensuring that in their decisions on issues related to end-user and consumer rights concerning publicly available electronic communications services, due consideration is given to consumer interests in electronic communications.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\n\n2. Where appropriate, interested parties may develop, with the guidance of national regulatory authorities, mechanisms, involving consumers, user groups and service providers, to improve the general quality of service provision by, inter alia, developing and monitoring codes of conduct and operating standards.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.23(b) (adapted)\n\n\n3. Without prejudice to national rules in conformity with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 law promoting cultural and media policy objectives, such as cultural and linguistic diversity and media pluralism, national regulatory authorities and other relevant authorities may promote cooperation between undertakings providing electronic communications networks and/or services and sectors interested in the promotion of lawful content in electronic communications networks and services. That cooperation may also include coordination of the public interest information to be provided pursuant to Article\u00a096(3) and Article\u00a095(1).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\n\nArticle 3425\n\n\nOut-of-court dispute resolution\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.24 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that \u00d6\u00a0consumers have access to\u00a0\u00d5 transparent, non-discriminatory, simple \u00d6\u00a0, fast, fair\u00a0\u00d5 and inexpensive out-of-court procedures are available for dealing with\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0their\u00a0\u00d5 unresolved disputes between consumers and\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0with\u00a0\u00d5 undertakings providing electronic communications networks and/or\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0publicly available electronic communications\u00a0\u00ef services \u00f0\u00a0other than number-independent interpersonal communications services,\u00a0\u00ef arising under this Directive and relating to the contractual conditions and/or performance of contracts concerning the supply of those \u00f0\u00a0networks and/or\u00a0\u00ef services. Member States shall adopt measures to ensure that\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0enable the national regulatory authority to act as a dispute settlement entity.\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0sSuch procedures \u00d6\u00a0shall comply with the quality requirements set out in Cchapter II of Directive 2013/11/EU.\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0enable disputes to be settled fairly and promptly and may, where warranted, adopt a system of reimbursement and/or compensation. Such procedures shall enable disputes to be settled impartially and shall not deprive the consumer of the legal protection afforded by national law. Member States may extend\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0grant access to such procedures\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0these obligations to cover disputes involving\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0to\u00a0\u00d5 other end-users \u00f0\u00a0, in particular micro and small enterprises.\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n2. Member States shall ensure that their legislation does not hamper the establishment of complaints offices and the provision of online services at the appropriate territorial level to facilitate access to dispute resolution by consumers and \u00d6\u00a0other\u00a0\u00d5 end-users. \u00f0\u00a0For disputes involving consumers and falling within the scope of Regulation\u00a0(EU)\u00a0524/2013, the provisions of that Regulation shall apply provided that the dispute settlement entity concerned has been notified to the Commission under Article 20 of Directive 2013/11/EU.\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0\n\n\n3. \u00d6\u00a0Without prejudice to the provisions of Directive 2013/11/EU,\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Wwhere such disputes involve parties in different Member States, Member States shall coordinate their efforts with a view to bringing about a resolution of the dispute.\n\n\n4. This Article is without prejudice to national court procedures.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\nArticle 2026\n\n\nDispute resolution between undertakings\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.22 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1. In the event of a dispute arising in connection with existing obligations under this Directive or the Specific Directives between undertakings providing electronic communications networks or services in a Member State, or between such undertakings and other undertakings in the Member State benefiting from obligations of access and/or interconnection \u00f0\u00a0or between undertakings providing electronic communications networks or services in a Member State and providers of associated facilities\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0arising under this Directive or the Specific Directives, the national regulatory authority concerned shall, at the request of either party, and without prejudice to the provisions of paragraph\u00a02, issue a binding decision to resolve the dispute in the shortest possible time frame and in any case within four months, except in exceptional circumstances. The Member State concerned shall require that all parties cooperate fully with the national regulatory authority.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\n2. Member States may make provision for national regulatory authorities to decline to resolve a dispute through a binding decision where other mechanisms, including mediation, exist and would better contribute to resolution of the dispute in a timely manner in accordance with the provisions of Article 38. The national regulatory authority shall inform the parties without delay. If after four months the dispute is not resolved, and if the dispute has not been brought before the courts by the party seeking redress, the national regulatory authority shall issue, at the request of either party, a binding decision to resolve the dispute in the shortest possible time frame and in any case within four months.\n\n\n3. In resolving a dispute, the national regulatory authority shall take decisions aimed at achieving the objectives set out in Article 38. Any obligations imposed on an undertaking by the national regulatory authority in resolving a dispute shall respect the provisions of this Directive or the Specific Directives.\n\n\n4. The decision of the national regulatory authority shall be made available to the public, having regard to the requirements of business confidentiality. The parties concerned shall be given a full statement of the reasons on which it is based.\n\n\n5. The procedure referred to in paragraphs 1, 3 and 4 shall not preclude either party from bringing an action before the courts.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.23 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a02127\n\n\nResolution of cross-border disputes\n\n\n1.\u00a0In the event of a cross-border dispute arising under this Directive or the Specific Directives between parties\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0undertakings\u00a0\u00d5 in different Member States, and where the dispute lies within the competence of national regulatory authorities from more than one Member State, the provisions set out in paragraphs\u00a02, 3 and\u00a04 shall be applicable. \u00f0\u00a0Those provisions shall not apply to disputes relating to radio spectrum coordination covered by Article 28. \u00ef\n\n\n2. Any party may refer the dispute to the national regulatory \u00d6\u00a0authority or\u00a0\u00d5 authorities concerned. The competent national regulatory \u00d6\u00a0authority or\u00a0\u00d5 authorities shall coordinate their efforts and shall have the right to consult\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0notify\u00a0the dispute to\u00ef BEREC in order to bring about a consistent resolution of the dispute, in accordance with the objectives set out in Article\u00a083.\n\n\n\n\nAny national regulatory authority which has competence in such a dispute may request BEREC to adopt an opinion as to the action to be taken in accordance with the provisions of the Framework Directive and/or the Specific Directives to resolve the dispute.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n3. BEREC shall issue an opinion indicating to the national regulatory authority or authorities concerned to take specific action in order to solve the dispute or to refrain from action, in the shortest possible time frame and in any case within four months, except in exceptional circumstances. \n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art 1.23\n\n\nWhere such a request has been made to BEREC, any national regulatory authority with competence in any aspect of the dispute shall await BEREC's opinion before taking action to resolve the dispute. This shall not preclude national regulatory authorities from taking urgent measures where necessary.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n\n4. The national regulatory authority or authorities concerned shall await BEREC's opinion before taking any action to solve the dispute.\u00a0In exceptional circumstances, where there is an urgent need to act, in order to safeguard competition or protect the interests of end-users, any of the competent national regulatory authorities may, either at the request of the parties or on its own initiative, adopt interim measures.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.23 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nAny obligations imposed by the national regulatory authority or authorities on undertakings as part of the resolution of a dispute shall comply with this Directive and the Specific Directives.\n\n\n5. Any obligations imposed on an undertaking by the national regulatory authority \u00d6\u00a0as part of the resolution of the\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0in resolving a dispute shall respect\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0comply with\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0the provisions of this Directive,\u00a0or the Specific Directives and take the utmost account of the opinion adopted by BEREC \u00f0\u00a0, and be adopted within one month from such opinion\u00a0\u00ef .\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.23 amended by Corrigendum, OJ L 241, 10.9.2013, p. 8\n\n\n3. Member States may make provision for the competent national regulatory authorities jointly to decline to resolve a dispute where other mechanisms, including mediation, exist and would better contribute to resolving the dispute in a timely manner in accordance with the provisions of Article 8.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.23\n\n\nThey shall inform the parties without delay. If after four months the dispute is not resolved, where the dispute has not been brought before the courts by the party seeking redress and if either party requests it, the national regulatory authorities shall coordinate their efforts in order to resolve the dispute, in accordance with the provisions set out in Article\u00a08 and taking the utmost account of any opinion adopted by BEREC.\n\n\n46. The procedure referred to in paragraph\u00a02 shall not preclude either party from bringing an action before the courts.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 28\n\n\nRadio Spectrum Coordination among Member States\n\n\n1. Member States and their competent authorities shall ensure that the use of radio spectrum is organised on their territory in a way that no other Member State is impeded, in particular due to cross-border harmful interference between Member States, from allowing on its territory the use of harmonised radio spectrum in accordance with Union legislation.\n\n\nThey shall take all necessary measures to this effect without prejudice to their obligations under international law and relevant international agreements such as the ITU Radio Regulations.\n\n\n2. Member States shall cooperate with each other, through the Radio Spectrum Policy Group, in the cross-border coordination of the use of radio spectrum in order to:\n\n\n(a) ensure compliance with paragraph 1; \n\n\n(b)solve any problem or dispute in relation to cross-border coordination or cross-border harmful interference.\n\n\n3. Any Member State concerned as well as the Commission may request the Radio Spectrum Policy Group to use its good offices and, where appropriate, to propose a coordinated solution in an opinion, in order to assist Member States in complying with paragraphs 1 and 2.\n\n\n4. At the request of a Member State or upon its own initiative, the Commission may, taking utmost account of the opinion of the Radio Spectrum Policy Group, adopt implementing measures to resolve cross-border harmful interferences between two or several Member States which prevent them from using the harmonised radio spectrum in their territory. Those implementing acts shall be adopted in accordance with the examination procedure referred to in Article 110(4).\n\n\nTitle III: Implementation\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.24 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a021a29\n\n\nPenalties\n\n\n\n\nMember States shall lay down rules on penalties \u00f0\u00a0, fines and periodic penalties, where necessary,\u00a0\u00ef applicable to infringements of national provisions adopted pursuant to this Directive \u00f0\u00a0or of any relevant legally binding decision of the national regulatory or other competent authority\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0and the Specific Directives and shall take all measures necessary to ensure that they are implemented. \u00f0\u00a0 Within the limits of national constitutional law, national regulatory and other competent authorities shall have the power to impose such penalties.\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0The penalties provided for must be appropriate, effective, proportionate and dissuasive. The Member States shall notify those provisions to the Commission by 25\u00a0May 2011\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0[date for transposition]\u00a0\u00d5 and shall notify it without delay of any subsequent amendment affecting them.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC Art.10 \n\n\nArticle 1030\n\n\nCompliance with the conditions of the general authorisation or of rights of use and with specific obligations\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 3.6(a) (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1. \u00f0\u00a0Member States shall ensure that their national regulatory and other competent authorities\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0National regulatory authorities\u00a0shall monitor and supervise compliance with the conditions of the general authorisation or of rights of use \u00f0\u00a0for radio spectrum and for numbers\u00a0\u00ef, and with the specific obligations referred to in Article 613(2), in accordance with Article 11\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and with the obligation to use radio spectrum effectively and efficiently in accordance with Articles 4, 45 and 47 paragraphs 1 and 2.\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0\n\n\nNational regulatory \u00f0 and other\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authorities shall have the power to require undertakings providing electronic communications networks or services covered by the general authorisation or enjoying rights of use for radio \u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0frequencies or numbers to provide all information necessary to verify compliance with the conditions of the general authorisation or of rights of use or with the specific obligations referred to in Article 613(2) \u00d6\u00a0or\u00a0 Article 47(1) and (2) \u00d5, in accordance with Article 1121.\n\n\n2. Where a national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority finds that an undertaking does not comply with one or more of the conditions of the general authorisation or of rights of use, or with the specific obligations referred to in Article 613(2), it shall notify the undertaking of those findings and give the undertaking the opportunity to state its views, within a reasonable time limit. \n\n\n3. The relevant authority shall have the power to require the cessation of the breach referred to in paragraph 2 either immediately or within a reasonable time limit and shall take appropriate and proportionate measures aimed at ensuring compliance.\n\n\nIn this regard, Member States shall empower the relevant authorities to impose:\n\n\n(a) dissuasive financial penalties where appropriate, which may include periodic penalties having retroactive effect; and\n\n\n(b) orders to cease or delay provision of a service or bundle of services which, if continued, would result in significant harm to competition, pending compliance with access obligations imposed following a market analysis carried out in accordance with Article 16\u00a065\u00a02002/21/EC (Framework Directive).\n\n\nThe measures and the reasons on which they are based shall be communicated to the undertaking concerned without delay and shall stipulate a reasonable period for the undertaking to comply with the measure.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 3.6(b) (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n4. Notwithstanding the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3, Member States shall empower the relevant authority to impose financial penalties where appropriate on undertakings for failure to provide information in accordance with the obligations imposed under Article 1121(1)(a) or (b) of this Directive and Article 9\u00a067\u00a0of\u00a0Directive 2002/19/EC (Access Directive) within a reasonable period stipulated by the national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 3.6(c) (adapted)\n\n\n5. In cases of serious \u00d6\u00a0breach\u00a0\u00d5 or repeated breaches of the conditions of the general authorisation or of the rights of use, or specific obligations referred to in Article 613(2) \u00d6\u00a0or\u00a0 Article 47 (1) or (2) \u00d5, where measures aimed at ensuring compliance as referred to in paragraph 3 of this Article have failed, \u00d6\u00a0Member States shall ensure that\u00a0\u00d5 national regulatory \u00d6\u00a0and other competent\u00a0\u00d5 authorities may prevent an undertaking from continuing to provide electronic communications networks or services or suspend or withdraw rights of use. \u00d6\u00a0Member States shall empower the relevant authority to impose\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0Ssanctions and penalties which are effective, proportionate and dissuasive. \u00d6\u00a0Such sanctions and penalties\u00a0\u00d5 may be applied to cover the period of any breach, even if the breach has subsequently been rectified.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 3.6(d) (adapted)\n\n\n6. Irrespective of the provisions of paragraphs 2, 3 and 5, where the relevant authority has evidence of a breach of the conditions of the general authorisation \u00d6\u00a0or of the\u00a0\u00d5 rights of use or of the specific obligations referred to in Article 613(2) \u00d6\u00a0or\u00a0 Article 47(1) and (2) \u00d5 that represents an immediate and serious threat to public safety, public security or public health or will create serious economic or operational problems for other providers or users of electronic communications networks or services or other users of the radio spectrum, it may take urgent interim measures to remedy the situation in advance of reaching a final decision. The undertaking concerned shall thereafter be given a reasonable opportunity to state its views and propose any remedies. Where appropriate, the relevant authority may confirm the interim measures, which shall be valid for a maximum of 3 months, but which may, in circumstances where enforcement procedures have not been completed, be extended for a further period of up to three months.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC (adapted)\n\n\n7. Undertakings shall have the right to appeal against measures taken under this Article in accordance with the procedure referred to in Article 4\u00a031 of \u00d6\u00a0this\u00a0\u00d5 Directive 2002/21/EC (Framework Directive).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\nArticle 431\n\n\nRight of appeal\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.4(a) \n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that effective mechanisms exist at national level under which any user or undertaking providing electronic communications networks and/or services who is affected by a decision of a national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority has the right of appeal against the decision to an appeal body that is \u00f0\u00a0completely\u00a0\u00ef independent of the parties involved \u00f0\u00a0and of any external intervention or political pressure liable to jeopardise its independent assessment of matters coming before it\u00a0\u00ef . This body, which may be a court, shall have the appropriate expertise to enable it to carry out its functions effectively. Member States shall ensure that the merits of the case are duly taken into account and that there is an effective appeal mechanism.\n\n\nPending the outcome of the appeal, the decision of the \u00f0 competent\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0national regulatory authority shall stand, unless interim measures are granted in accordance with national law.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\n\n\n2. Where the appeal body referred to in paragraph 1 is not judicial in character, written reasons for its decision shall always be given. Furthermore, in such a case, its decision shall be subject to review by a court or tribunal within the meaning of Article 267 of the Treaty.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.4(b)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n3. Member States shall collect information on the general subject matter of appeals, the number of requests for appeal, the duration of the appeal proceedings and the number of decisions to grant interim measures. Member States shall provide such information, \u00f0\u00a0as well as the decisions or judgments\u00a0\u00ef to the Commission and BEREC after a reasoned request from either.\n\n\nTitle IV: Internal market procedures\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.6 (adapted)\n\n\nArticle\u00a0732\n\n\nConsolidating the internal market for electronic communications\n\n\n1. In carrying out their tasks under this Directive and the Specific Directives, national regulatory authorities shall take the utmost account of the objectives set out in Article\u00a08\u00a03, including in so far as they relate to the functioning of the internal market.\n\n\n2. National regulatory authorities shall contribute to the development of the internal market by working with each other and with the Commission and BEREC in a transparent manner so as to ensure the consistent application, in all Member States, of the provisions of this Directive and the Specific Directives. To this end, they shall, in particular, work with the Commission and BEREC to identify the types of instruments and remedies best suited to address particular types of situations in the marketplace.\n\n\n3. Except where otherwise provided in recommendations or guidelines adopted pursuant to Article\u00a07b\u00a034 upon completion of the consultation referred to in Article\u00a06\u00a023, where a national regulatory authority intends to take a measure which:\n\n\n(a) falls within the scope of Articles\u00a0\u00d6\u00a059, 62, 65 or 66\u00a0\u00d5\u00a015 or\u00a016 of this Directive, or Articles\u00a05 or\u00a08 of Directive 2002/19/EC (Access Directive); and\n\n\n(b) would affect trade between Member States;\n\n\nit shall make the draft measure accessible to the Commission, BEREC, and the national regulatory authorities in other Member States, at the same time, together with the reasoning on which the measure is based, in accordance with Article\u00a0520(3), and inform the Commission, BEREC and other national regulatory authorities thereof. National regulatory authorities, BEREC and the Commission may make comments to the national regulatory authority concerned only within one month. The one-month period may not be extended.\n\n\n4. Where an intended measure covered by paragraph\u00a03 aims at:\n\n\n(a) defining a relevant market which differs from those defined in the Recommendation in accordance with Article\u00a015\u00a062(1); or\n\n\n(b) deciding whether or not to designate an undertaking as having, either individually or jointly with others, significant market power, under Article\u00a01665(3) or\u00a0(5) (4);\n\n\nand would affect trade between Member States, and the Commission has indicated to the national regulatory authority that it considers that the draft measure would create a barrier to the single market or if it has serious doubts as to its compatibility with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 law and in particular the objectives referred to in Article\u00a083, the draft measure shall not be adopted for a further two months. This period may not be extended. The Commission shall inform other national regulatory authorities of its reservations in such a case.\n\n\n\n\n5. Within the two-month period referred to in paragraph\u00a04, the Commission may:\n\n\n(a) take a decision requiring the national regulatory authority concerned to withdraw the draft measure; and/or\n\n\n(b) take a decision to lift its reservations in relation to a draft measure referred to in paragraph\u00a04.\n\n\nThe Commission shall take utmost account of the opinion of BEREC before issuing a decision. The decision shall be accompanied by a detailed and objective analysis of why the Commission considers that the draft measure should not be adopted, together with specific proposals for amending the draft measure.\n\n\n6. Where the Commission has adopted a decision in accordance with paragraph\u00a05, requiring the national regulatory authority to withdraw a draft measure, the national regulatory authority shall amend or withdraw the draft measure within six months of the date of the Commission's decision. When the draft measure is amended, the national regulatory authority shall undertake a public consultation in accordance with the procedures referred to in Article\u00a0623, and shall re-notify the amended draft measure to the Commission in accordance with the provisions of paragraph\u00a03.\n\n\n7. The national regulatory authority concerned shall take the utmost account of comments of other national regulatory authorities, BEREC and the Commission and may, except in cases covered by paragraphs\u00a04 and\u00a05(a), adopt the resulting draft measure and, where it does so, shall communicate it to the Commission.\n\n\n8. The national regulatory authority shall communicate to the Commission and BEREC all adopted final measures which fall under Article\u00a07\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0paragraph\u00a0\u00d5 (3)(a) and\u00a0(b) \u00d6\u00a0of this Article\u00a0\u00d5 . \n\n\n9. In exceptional circumstances, where a national regulatory authority considers that there is an urgent need to act, in order to safeguard competition and protect the interests of users, by way of derogation from the procedure set out in paragraphs\u00a03 and\u00a04, it may immediately adopt proportionate and provisional measures. It shall, without delay, communicate those measures, with full reasons, to the Commission, the other national regulatory authority, and BEREC. A decision by the national regulatory authority to render such measures permanent or extend the time for which they are applicable shall be subject to the provisions of paragraphs\u00a03 and\u00a04.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.7 (adapted)\n\n\nArticle\u00a07a33\n\n\nProcedure for the consistent application of remedies\n\n\n1. Where an intended measure covered by Article\u00a0732(3) aims at imposing, amending or withdrawing an obligation on an operator in application of Article\u00a016\u00a065 in conjunction with Article\u00a05\u00a059 and Articles\u00a0967 to\u00a013\u00a074\u00a0of Directive 2002/19/EC (Access Directive), and Article\u00a017 of Directive 2002/22/EC (Universal Service Directive), the Commission may, within the period of one month provided for by Article\u00a0732(3) of  this Directive, notify the national regulatory authority concerned and BEREC of its reasons for considering that the draft measure would create a barrier to the single market or its serious doubts as to its compatibility with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 law. In such a case, the draft measure shall not be adopted for a further three months following the Commission's notification.\n\n\nIn the absence of such notification, the national regulatory authority concerned may adopt the draft measure, taking utmost account of any comments made by the Commission, BEREC or any other national regulatory authority.\n\n\n2. Within the three month period referred to in paragraph\u00a01, the Commission, BEREC and the national regulatory authority concerned shall cooperate closely to identify the most appropriate and effective measure in the light of the objectives laid down in Article\u00a083, whilst taking due account of the views of market participants and the need to ensure the development of consistent regulatory practice.\n\n\n3. Within six weeks from the beginning of the three month period referred to in paragraph\u00a01, BEREC shall, acting by a majority of its component members, issue an opinion on the Commission's notification referred to in paragraph\u00a01, indicating whether it considers that the draft measure should be amended or withdrawn and, where appropriate, provide specific proposals to that end. This opinion shall be reasoned and made public.\n\n\n4. If in its opinion, BEREC shares the serious doubts of the Commission, it shall cooperate closely with the national regulatory authority concerned to identify the most appropriate and effective measure. Before the end of the three month period referred in paragraph\u00a01, the national regulatory authority may:\n\n\n(a) amend or withdraw its draft measure taking utmost account of the Commission's notification referred to in paragraph\u00a01 and of BEREC's opinion and advice;\n\n\n(b) maintain its draft measure.\n\n\n5. Where BEREC does not share the serious doubts of the Commission or does not issue an opinion, or where the national regulatory authority amends or maintains its draft measure pursuant to paragraph\u00a04,\u00a0tThe Commission may, within one month following the end of the three month period referred to in paragraph\u00a01 and taking utmost account of the opinion of BEREC if any:\n\n\n\n\n(a) issue a recommendation requiring the national regulatory authority concerned to amend or withdraw the draft measure, including specific proposals to that end and providing reasons justifying its recommendation, in particular where BEREC does not share the serious doubts of the Commission;\n\n\n(b) take a decision to lift its reservations indicated in accordance with paragraph\u00a01.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(c) take a decision requiring the national regulatory authority concerned to withdraw the draft measure, where BEREC shares the serious doubts of the Commission. The decision shall be accompanied by a detailed and objective analysis of why the Commission considers that the draft measure should not be adopted, together with specific proposals for amending the draft measure. In this case, the procedure referred to in Article 32 (6) shall apply mutatis mutandis.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.7  (adapted)\n\n\n6. Within one month of the Commission issuing the recommendation in accordance with paragraph\u00a05(a) or lifting its reservations in accordance with paragraph\u00a05(b) \u00d6\u00a0of this Article\u00a0\u00d5 , the national regulatory authority concerned shall communicate to the Commission and BEREC the adopted final measure.\n\n\nThis period may be extended to allow the national regulatory authority to undertake a public consultation in accordance with Article\u00a0623.\n\n\n7. Where the national regulatory authority decides not to amend or withdraw the draft measure on the basis of the recommendation issued under paragraph\u00a05(a), it shall provide a reasoned justification.\n\n\n8. The national regulatory authority may withdraw the proposed draft measure at any stage of the procedure.\n\n\nArticle\u00a07b34\n\n\nImplementing provisions\n\n\n1. After public consultation and consultation with national regulatory authorities and taking utmost account of the opinion of BEREC, the Commission may adopt recommendations and/or guidelines in relation to Article\u00a0732 that define the form, content and level of detail to be given in the notifications required in accordance with Article\u00a0732(3), the circumstances in which notifications would not be required, and the calculation of the time-limits.\n\n\n2. The measures referred to in paragraph\u00a01 shall be adopted in accordance with the advisory procedure referred to in Article\u00a022(2).\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nCHAPTER II\n\n\nconsistent spectrum assignement\n\n\nArticle 35\n\n\n\n\nPeer review process\n\n\n1. As regards the management of radio spectrum, national regulatory authorities shall be entrusted with the powers to at least adopt the following measures::\n\n\n(a)in case of individual rights of use for radio spectrum, the selection process, in relation to Article 54;\n\n\n(b)the criteria regarding the eligibility of the bidder, where appropriate, in relation to Article 48 (4);\n\n\n(c)the parameters of spectrum economic valuation measures, such as the reserve price, in relation to Article 42;\n\n\n(d)the duration of the rights of use and the conditions for renewal in line with Articles 49 and Article 50;\n\n\n(e)any measures to promote competition pursuant to Article 52, when necessary; \n\n\n(f)the conditions related to the assignment, transfer, including trade and lease of rights of use for radio spectrum in relation to Article 51, sharing of spectrum or wireless infrastructure in relation to Article 59 paragraph 3 or the accumulation of rights of use in relation to Article 52 paragraph 2 (c) and (e); and\n\n\n(g)the parameters of coverage conditions pursuant to overall Member State policy objectives in this respect, in relation to Article 47.\n\n\nWhen adopting these measures, the national regulatory authority shall take into account the relevant national policy objectives set out by the Member State as well as other relevant national measures in regard to the management of radio spectrum in compliance with Union law and shall base its measure on a thorough and objective assessment of the competitive, technical and economic situation of the market. \n\n\n2. Where a national regulatory authority intends to take a measure which falls within the scope of paragraph 1 (a) to (g), it shall make the draft measure accessible, together with the reasoning on which the measure is based, to BEREC, the Commission and national regulatory authorities in other Member States, at the same time. \n\n\n3. Within one month, or a longer period, if the national regulatory authority agrees to extend the deadline, BEREC shall issue a reasoned opinion on the draft measure, which shall analyse whether that measure would be the most appropriate in order to: \n\n\n(a)promote the development of the internal market as well as competition and maximise the benefits for the consumer, and overall achieve the objectives and principles set in Articles 3 and 45(2),\n\n\n(b)ensure effective and efficient use of radio spectrum; and\n\n\n(c)ensure stable and predictable investment conditions for existing and prospective radio spectrum users when deploying networks for the provision of electronic communications services which rely on radio spectrum.\n\n\nThe reasoned opinion shall state if the draft measure should be amended or withdrawn.Where appropriate, BEREC shall provide specific recommendations to that end. National regulatory authorities and the Commission may also make comments on the draft decision to the national regulatory authority concerned.\n\n\n4. When carrying out their tasks pursuant to this Article, BEREC and national regulatory authorities shall have regard in particular to:\n\n\n(a)the objectives and principles provided in this Directive; as well as to any relevant Commission implementing decision adopted in accordance with this Directive as well as Decisions 676/2002/EC and 243/2012/EC;\n\n\n(b)any specific national objectives established by the Member State consistent with Union law; \n\n\n(c)the need to avoid that competition is distorted when adopting such measures;\n\n\n\n\n(d)the results of the most recent geographical survey of networks pursuant to Article 22;\n\n\n(e)the need to ensure coherence with recent and pending assignment procedures in other Member States, and possible effects on trade between Member States; and\n\n\n(f)any relevant opinion of the Radio Spectrum Policy Group.\n\n\n5. The national regulatory authority concerned shall take utmost account of the opinion of BEREC and of comments made by the Commission and other national regulatory authorities before adopting its final decision. It shall communicate the final decision adopted to BEREC and the Commission. \n\n\nWhere the national regulatory authority decides not to amend or withdraw the draft measure on the basis of the reasoned opinion issued pursuant to paragraph 2 of this Article, it shall provide a reasoned justification. \n\n\nThe national regulatory authority concerned may withdraw its draft measure at any stage of the procedure.\n\n\n6. When preparing their draft measure pursuant to this Article, national regulatory authorities may seek support from BEREC.\n\n\n7. BEREC, the Commission and the national regulatory authority concerned shall cooperate closely to identify the most appropriate and effective solution in the light of the regulatory objectives and principles laid down in this Directive whilst taking due account of the views of market participants and the need to ensure the development of consistent regulatory practice. \n\n\n8. The final decision adopted by the national regulatory authority shall be published.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 836\n\n\nHarmonised assignment of radio frequencies\n\n\nWhere the usage of radio frequencies has been harmonised, access conditions and procedures have been agreed, and undertakings to which the radio frequencies shall be assigned have been selected in accordance with international agreements and Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 rules, Member States shall grant the right of use for such radio frequencies in accordance therewith. Provided that all national conditions attached to the right to use the radio frequencies concerned have been satisfied in the case of a common selection procedure, Member States shall not impose any further conditions, additional criteria or procedures which would restrict, alter or delay the correct implementation of the common assignment of such radio frequencies.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 37\n\n\nJoint authorisation process to grant individual rights of use for radio spectrum\n\n\n1. Two or several Member States may cooperate with each other and with the Commission and BEREC to  meet their obligations under Articles 13, 46 and 54, by jointly establishing the common aspects of an authorisation process and also jointly conducting the selection process to grant individual rights of use for radio spectrum in line, where applicable with any common timetable established in accordance with Article 53. The joint authorisation process shall meet the following criteria:\n\n\n(a)the individual national authorisation processes shall be initiated and implemented by the competent authorities according to a jointly agreed schedule;\n\n\n\n\n(b)it shall provide where appropriate for common conditions and procedures for the selection and granting of individual rights among the Member States concerned;\n\n\n(c)it shall provide where appropriate for common or comparable conditions to be attached to the individual rights of use among the Member States concerned inter alia allowing users to be assigned similar radio spectrum blocks;\n\n\n(d)it shall be open at any time until the authorisation process has been conducted to other Member States.\n\n\n2. Where the measures taken for the purposes of paragraph (1) fall in the scope of Article 35(1), the procedure provided in that Article shall  be followed by the national regulatory authorities concerned simultaneously. \n\n\nCHAPTER III\n\n\nharmonisation procedures\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.21 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a01938\n\n\nHarmonisation procedures\n\n\n1. Without prejudice to Article \u00d6\u00a0s\u00a0\u00d5\u00a09\u00a0\u00d6\u00a037, 45, 46(3), 47(3), 53\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0of this Directive and Articles\u00a06 and\u00a08 of Directive 2002/20/EC (Authorisation Directive), where the Commission finds that divergences in the implementation by the national regulatory authorities \u00f0\u00a0or by other competent authorities\u00a0\u00ef of the regulatory tasks specified in this Directive and the Specific Directives may create a barrier to the internal market, the Commission may, taking the utmost account of the opinion of BEREC, issue a recommendation or a decision on the harmonised application of the provisions in this Directive and the Specific Directives in order to further the achievement of the objectives set out in Article\u00a038.\n\n\n2. Where the Commission issues a recommendation pursuant to paragraph\u00a01, it shall act in accordance with the advisory procedure referred to in Article\u00a022(2).\n\n\nMember States shall ensure that national regulatory \u00f0\u00a0and other competent\u00a0\u00ef authorities take the utmost account of those recommendations \u00d6\u00a0pursuant to paragraph 1\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0in carrying out their tasks. Where a national regulatory authority \u00f0\u00a0or other competent authority\u00a0\u00ef chooses not to follow a recommendation, it shall inform the Commission, giving the reasons for its position.\n\n\n3. The decisions adopted pursuant to paragraph\u00a01\u00a0may include only the identification of a harmonised or coordinated approach for the purposes of addressing the following matters:\n\n\n(a)the inconsistent implementation of general regulatory approaches by national regulatory authorities on the regulation of electronic communication\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0communications\u00a0\u00d5 markets in the application of Articles\u00a015\u00a062 and\u00a016\u00a065, where it creates a barrier to the internal market. Such decisions shall not refer to specific notifications issued by the national regulatory authorities pursuant to Article\u00a07a33;\n\n\nIn such a case, the Commission shall propose a draft decision only:\n\n\n\u2013after at least two years following the adoption of a Commission Recommendation dealing with the same matter, and\n\n\n\u2013taking utmost account of an opinion from BEREC on the case for adoption of such a decision, which shall be provided by BEREC within three months of the Commission's request;\n\n\n\n\n\n(b)numbering, including number ranges, portability of numbers and identifiers, number and address translation systems, and access to\u00a0112 emergency services.\n\n\n4. The decision referred to in paragraph\u00a01, designed to amend non-essential elements of this Directive by supplementing it, shall be adopted in accordance with the regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0examination\u00a0\u00ef procedure with scrutiny referred to in Article\u00a022(3)110(4).\n\n\n5. BEREC may on its own initiative advise the Commission on whether a measure should be adopted pursuant to paragraph\u00a01.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.19(a)\n\n\nArticle 1739\n\n\nStandardisation\n\n\n1. The Commission, acting in accordance with the procedure referred to in Article 22(2), shall draw up and publish in the Official Journal of the European UnionCommunities a list of \u00e81\u00a0non-compulsory standards\u00a0\u00e7 and/or specifications to serve as a basis for encouraging the harmonised provision of electronic communications networks, electronic communications services and associated facilities and services. Where necessary, the Commission may, acting in accordance with the procedure referred to in Article 22(2) and following consultation of the Committee established by Directive 2015/1535/EU\u00a098/34/EC, request that standards be drawn up by the European standards organisations (European Committee for Standardisation (CEN), European Committee for Electrotechnical Standardisation (CENELEC), and European Telecommunications Standards Institute (ETSI)).\n\n\n2. Member States shall encourage the use of the standards and/or specifications referred to in paragraph 1, for the provision of services, technical interfaces and/or network functions, to the extent strictly necessary to ensure interoperability of services and to improve freedom of choice for users.\n\n\nAs long as standards and/or specifications have not been published in accordance with paragraph 1, Member States shall encourage the implementation of standards and/or specifications adopted by the European standards organisations.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.19(b)\n\n\nIn the absence of such standards and/or specifications, Member States shall encourage the implementation of international standards or recommendations adopted by the International Telecommunication Union (ITU), the European Conference of Postal and Telecommunications Administrations (CEPT), the International Organisation for Standardisation (ISO) and the International Electrotechnical Commission (IEC).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\nWhere international standards exist, Member States shall encourage the European standards organisations to use them, or the relevant parts of them, as a basis for the standards they develop, except where such international standards or relevant parts would be ineffective.\n\n\n3. If the standards and/or specifications referred to in paragraph 1 have not been adequately implemented so that interoperability of services in one or more Member States cannot be ensured, the implementation of such standards and/or specifications may be made compulsory under the procedure laid down in paragraph 4, to the extent strictly necessary to ensure such interoperability and to improve freedom of choice for users.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.19(c)\n\n\n\n\n4. Where the Commission intends to make the implementation of certain standards and/or specifications compulsory, it shall publish a notice in the Official Journal of the European Union and invite public comment by all parties concerned. The Commission shall take appropriate implementing measures and make implementation of the relevant standards compulsory by making reference to them as compulsory standards in the list of standards and/or specifications published in the Official Journal of the European Union.\n\n\n5. Where the Commission considers that standards and/or specifications referred to in paragraph\u00a01 no longer contribute to the provision of harmonised electronic communications services, or that they no longer meet consumers' needs or are hampering technological development, it shall,\u00a0acting in accordance with the advisory procedure referred to in Article\u00a022(2), remove them from the list of standards and/or specifications referred to in paragraph\u00a01.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.19(d) \n\n\n6. Where the Commission considers that standards and/or specifications referred to in paragraph 4 no longer contribute to the provision of harmonised electronic communications services, or that they no longer meet consumers' needs or are hampering technological development, it shall \u00e81\u00a0take the appropriate implementing measures and remove those standards and/or specifications from the list of standards and/or specifications referred to in paragraph 1\u00a0\u00e7 .\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.19(e) (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n6a7. The implementing measures designed to amend non-essential elements of this Directive by supplementing it, referred to in paragraphs\u00a04 and\u00a06, shall be adopted in accordance with the regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0examination\u00a0\u00ef procedure with scrutiny referred to in Article\u00a0110(4)22(3).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\n78. This Article does not apply in respect of any of the essential requirements, interface specifications or harmonised standards to which the provisions of Directive 2014/53/EU\u00a01999/5/EC apply.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 18\n\n\nInteroperability of digital interactive television services\n\n\n1. In order to promote the free flow of information, media pluralism and cultural diversity, Member States shall encourage, in accordance with the provisions of Article 17(2):\n\n\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0(a) providers of digital interactive television services for distribution to the public in the Community on digital interactive television platforms, regardless of the transmission mode, to use an open API;\n\n\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0(b) providers of all enhanced digital television equipment deployed for the reception of digital interactive television services on interactive digital television platforms to comply with an open API in accordance with the minimum requirements of the relevant standards or specifications;\n\n\n\n\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0(c) providers of digital TV services and equipment to cooperate in the provision of interoperable TV services for disabled end-users.\n\n\n2. Without prejudice to Article 5(1)(b) of Directive 2002/19/ EC (Access Directive), Member States shall encourage proprietors of APIs to make available on fair, reasonable and non-discriminatory terms, and against appropriate remuneration, all such information as is necessary to enable providers of digital interactive television services to provide all services supported by the API in a fully functional form.\n\n\nTitle V: Security and integrity\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.15 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a013a40\n\n\nSecurity and integrity\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0of networks and services\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that undertakings providing public communications networks or publicly available electronic communications services take appropriate technical and organisational measures to appropriately manage the risks posed to security of networks and services. Having regard to the state of the art, these measures shall ensure a level of security appropriate to the risk presented. In particular, measures shall be taken to prevent and minimise the impact of security incidents on users and interconnected\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0on other\u00a0\u00ef networks \u00f0\u00a0and services\u00a0\u00ef.\n\n\n2. Member States shall ensure that undertakings providing public communications networks take all appropriate steps to guarantee the integrity of their networks, and thus ensure the continuity of supply of services provided over those networks.\n\n\n3. Member States shall ensure that undertakings providing public communications networks or publicly available electronic communications services notify \u00f0\u00a0without undue delay\u00a0\u00ef the competent national regulatory authority of a breach of security or loss of integrity that has had a significant impact on the operation of networks or services.\n\n\nIn order to determine the significance of the impact of a security incident, the following parameters shall, in particular, be taken into account: \n\n\n(a)the number of users affected by the breach; \n\n\n(b)the duration of the breach; \n\n\n(c)the geographical spread of the area affected by the breach;\n\n\n(d)the extent to which the functioning of the service is disrupted;\n\n\n(e)the impact on economic and societal activities.\n\n\nWhere appropriate, the national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority concerned shall inform the national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authorities in other Member States and the European Network and Information Security Agency (ENISA). The national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority concerned may inform the public or require the undertakings to do so, where it determines that disclosure of the breach is in the public interest.\n\n\nOnce a year, the national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority concerned shall submit a summary report to the Commission and ENISA on the notifications received and the action taken in accordance with this paragraph. \n\n\n4. The Commission, taking the utmost account of the opinion of ENISA, may adopt appropriate technical implementing measures with a view to harmonising the measures referred to in paragraphs\u00a01, 2, and\u00a03, including measures defining the circumstances, format and procedures applicable to notification requirements. These technical implementing measures shall be based on European and international standards to the greatest extent possible, and shall not prevent Member States from adopting additional requirements in order to pursue the objectives set out in paragraphs\u00a01 and\u00a02.\n\n\n\n\nThese implementing measures, designed to amend non-essential elements of this Directive by supplementing it, shall be adopted in accordance with the regulatory procedure with scrutiny referred to in Article\u00a022(3).\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n4. This Article is without prejudice to Regulation (EU) 2016/679 on the protection of natural persons with regard to the processing of personal data and on the free movement of such data and Directive 2002/58/EC concerning the processing of personal data and the protection of  privacy in the electronic communications sector.\n\n\n5. The Commission, shall be empowered to adopt delegated acts in accordance with Article 109 with a view to specifying the measures referred to in paragraphs\u00a01 and 2, including measures defining the circumstances, format and procedures applicable to notification requirements. The delegated acts shall be based on European and international standards to the greatest extent possible, and shall not prevent Member States from adopting additional requirements in order to pursue the objectives set out in paragraphs\u00a01 and\u00a02.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.15 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a013b41\n\n\nImplementation and enforcement\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that in order to implement Article\u00a013a40, \u00d6\u00a0the \u00d5 competent national regulatory authorities have the power to issue binding instructions, including those regarding \u00f0\u00a0the measures required to remedy a breach and\u00a0\u00ef time-limits for implementation, to undertakings providing public communications networks or publicly available electronic communications services.\n\n\n2. Member States shall ensure that competent national regulatory authorities have the power to require undertakings providing public communications networks or publicly available electronic communications services to:\n\n\n(a) provide information needed to assess the security and/or integrity of their services and networks, including documented security policies; and\n\n\n(b) submit to a security audit carried out by a qualified independent body or a competent national authority and make the results thereof available to the national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority. The cost of the audit shall be paid by the undertaking.\n\n\n3. Member States shall ensure that national regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0the competent\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0 authorities have all the powers necessary to investigate cases of non-compliance and the effects thereof on the security and integrity of the networks \u00d6\u00a0and services\u00a0\u00d5 .\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n4. Member States shall ensure that, in order to implement Article 40, the competent authorities have the power to obtain the assistance of Computer Security Incident Response Teams ('CSIRTs') under Article 9 of Directive (EU) 2016/1148/EU in relation to issues falling within the tasks of the CSIRTs pursuant to Annex I, point 2 of that Directive.\n\n\n5. The competent authorities shall, whenever appropriate and in accordance with national law, consult and cooperate with the relevant national law enforcement authorities, the competent authorities as defined in Article 8 (1) of Directive (EU) 2016/1148 and the national data protection authorities.  \n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.15 \n\n\n4. These provisions shall be without prejudice to Article\u00a03 of this Directive.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC\n\n\nArticle 13\n\n\nFees for rights of use and rights to install facilities\n\n\nMember States may allow the relevant authority to impose fees for the rights of use for radio frequencies or numbers or rights to install facilities on, over or under public or private property which reflect the need to ensure the optimal use of these resources. Member States shall ensure that such fees shall be objectively justified, transparent, non-discriminatory and proportionate in relation to their intended purpose and shall take into account the objectives in Article 8 of Directive 2002/21/EC (Framework Directive).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\u00d6\u00a0Part II. NETWORKS\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n\u00d6\u00a0Title I: Market entry and deployment\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nArticle 13\u00a042\n\n\nFees for rights of use \u00d6\u00a0for radio spectrum\u00a0\u00d5 and rights to install facilities\n\n\nMember States may allow the relevant\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00d5 authority to impose fees for the rights of use for radio frequencies\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0or numbers or rights to install facilities on, over or under public or private property \u00f0\u00a0that are used for the provision of electronic communications services or networks and associated facilities\u00a0\u00ef which reflect the need to ensure the optimal use of these resources. Member States shall ensure that such fees shall be objectively justified, transparent, non-discriminatory and proportionate in relation to their intended purpose and shall take into account the objectives in Articles\u00a03, 4 and 45(2)\u00a08 of Directive 2002/21/EC (Framework Directive).\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0, as well as:\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(a)being service and technology neutral, subject only to limitations in line with Article 45(4) and (5), while promoting the effective and efficient use of spectrum and maximising social and economic utility of spectrum;\n\n\n(a)taking into account the need to foster the development of innovative services; and\n\n\n(b)taking into account possible alternative uses of the resources.\n\n\n\n\n2. Member States shall ensure that reserve prices established as minimum fees for rights of use for radio spectrum reflect the additional costs entailed by conditions attached to these rights in pursuit of the objectives under Articles 3, 4 and 45(2), such as coverage obligations that would fall outside normal commercial standards, in accordance with paragraph 1.\n\n\n3. Member States shall apply payment modalities linked to the actual availability of the radio spectrum in question, which do not unduly burden any additional investments in networks and associated facilities necessary for the efficient use of the radio spectrum and the provision of related services.\n\n\n4. Member States shall ensure that where competent authorities impose fees, they take into account other fees or administrative charges linked to the general authorisation or rights of use established pursuant to this Directive, in order not to create undue financial burden to undertakings providing electronic communications networks and services and to incentivise optimal use of the allocated resources.\n\n\n5. The imposition of fees pursuant to this Article shall comply with the requirements of Article 23 and, where applicable, Articles 35, 48(6) and 54.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\n\nCHAPTER I \n\n\n\u00d6\u00a0ACCESS TO LAND\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\nArticle 1143\n\n\nRights of way\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that when a competent authority considers:\n\n\n\u2013an application for the granting of rights to install facilities on, over or under public or private property to an undertaking authorised to provide public communications networks, or\n\n\n\u2013an application for the granting of rights to install facilities on, over or under public property to an undertaking authorised to provide electronic communications networks other than to the public,\n\n\nthe competent authority:\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.13(a)\n\n\n\u2013acts on the basis of simple, efficient, transparent and publicly available procedures, applied without discrimination and without delay, and in any event makes its decision within six months of the application, except in cases of expropriation, and\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\n\u2013follows the principles of transparency and non-discrimination in attaching conditions to any such rights.\n\n\nThe abovementioned procedures can differ depending on whether the applicant is providing public communications networks or not.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.13(b)\n\n\n2. Member States shall ensure that where public or local authorities retain ownership or control of undertakings operating public electronic communications networks and/or publicly available electronic communications services, there is an effective structural separation of the function responsible for granting the rights referred to in paragraph\u00a01 from the activities associated with ownership or control.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\n3. Member States shall ensure that effective mechanisms exist to allow undertakings to appeal against decisions on the granting of rights to install facilities to a body that is independent of the parties involved.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.14\n\n\nArticle\u00a012\n\n\nCo-location and sharing of network elements and associated facilities for providers of electronic communications networks\n\n\n1. Where an undertaking providing electronic communications networks has the right under national legislation to install facilities on, over or under public or private property, or may take advantage of a procedure for the expropriation or use of property, national regulatory authorities shall, taking full account of the principle of  proportionality, be able to impose the sharing of such facilities or property, including buildings, entries to buildings, building wiring, masts, antennae, towers and other supporting constructions, ducts, conduits, manholes, cabinets.\n\n\n2. Member States may require holders of the rights referred to in paragraph\u00a01 to share facilities or property (including physical co-location) or take measures to facilitate the coordination of public works in order to protect the environment, public health, public security or to meet town and country planning objectives and only after an appropriate period of public consultation, during which all interested parties shall be given an opportunity to express their views. Such sharing or coordination arrangements may include rules for apportioning the costs of facility or property sharing.\n\n\n3. Member States shall ensure that national authorities, after an appropriate period of public consultation during which all interested parties are given the opportunity to state their views, also have the power to impose obligations in relation to the sharing of wiring inside buildings or up to the first concentration or distribution point where this is located outside the building, on the holders of the rights referred to in paragraph\u00a01 and/or on the owner of such wiring, where this is justified on the grounds that duplication of such infrastructure would be economically inefficient or physically impracticable. Such sharing or coordination arrangements may include rules for apportioning the costs of facility or property sharing adjusted for risk where appropriate.\n\n\n4. Member States shall ensure that competent national authorities may require undertakings to provide the necessary information, if requested by the competent authorities, in order for these authorities, in conjunction with national regulatory authorities, to be able to establish a detailed inventory of the nature, availability and geographical location of the facilities referred to in paragraph\u00a01 and make it available to interested parties.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\nArticle\u00a044\n\n\nCo-location and sharing of network elements and associated facilities for providers of electronic communications networks\n\n\n1. Where an operator has exercised the right under national legislation to install facilities on, over or under public or private property, or has taken advantage of a procedure for the expropriation or use of property, competent authorities shall, be able to impose co-location and sharing of the network elements and associated facilities installed, in order to protect the environment, public health, public security or to meet town and country planning objectives. Co-location or sharing of networks elements and facilities installed and sharing of property may only be imposed after an appropriate period of public consultation, during which all interested parties shall be given an opportunity to express their views and only in the specific areas where such sharing is deemed necessary in view of pursuing the objectives provided in this Article. Competent authorities shall be able to impose the sharing of such facilities or property, including land, buildings, entries to buildings, building wiring, masts, antennae, towers and other supporting constructions, ducts, conduits, manholes, cabinets or measures facilitating the coordination of public works. Where necessary, national regulatory authorities shall provide rules for apportioning the costs of facility or property sharing and of civil works coordination.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.14 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n52. Measures taken by a national\u00a0regulatory\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0competent\u00a0\u00ef authority in accordance with this Article shall be objective, transparent, non-discriminatory, and proportionate. Where relevant, these measures shall be carried out in coordination with \u00d6\u00a0the\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0local\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0national regulatory\u00a0\u00ef authorities.\n\n\n\nCHAPTER II\n\n\nACCESS TO RADIO SPECTRUM\n\n\nSection 1 Authorisations\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Art. 1.10 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a0945\n\n\nManagement of radio \u00d6\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0frequenciesfor electronic communications services\n\n\n1. Taking due account of the fact that radio frequencies are\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum is\u00a0\u00ef a public good that has an important social, cultural and economic value, Member States shall ensure the effective management of radio frequencies\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef for electronic communications services \u00f0\u00a0and networks\u00a0\u00ef in their territory in accordance with Articles\u00a083 and 48a. They shall ensure that \u00f0\u00a0radio\u00a0\u00ef spectrum allocation used for electronic communications services \u00f0\u00a0and networks\u00a0\u00ef and issuing general authorisations or individual rights of use of\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0for\u00a0\u00d5 such radio frequencies\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef by competent national authorities are based on objective, transparent, non-discriminatory and proportionate criteria.\n\n\nIn applying this Article, Member States shall respect relevant international agreements, including the ITU Radio Regulations\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0and other agreements adopted in the framework of the ITU\u00a0\u00ef, and may take public policy considerations into account.\n\n\n2. Member States shall promote the harmonisation of use of radio frequencies\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef across the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 , consistent with the need to ensure effective and efficient use thereof and in pursuit of benefits for the consumer such as economies of scale and interoperability of services \u00d6\u00a0and networks\u00a0\u00d5 . In so doing, they shall act in accordance with Article\u00a08a\u00a04 and with the Decision No\u00a0676/2002/EC (Radio Spectrum Decision)\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0by inter alia\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0:. \n\n\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n(a)ensuring coverage of their national territory and population at high quality and speed, both indoors and outdoors, including along major transport paths, including the trans-European transport network;\n\n\n(b)ensuring that areas with similar characteristics, in particular in terms of network deployment or population density, are subject to consistent coverage conditions;\n\n\n(c)facilitating the rapid development in the Union of new wireless communications technologies and applications, including, where appropriate, in a cross-sectorial approach;\n\n\n(d)ensuring the prevention of cross-border or national harmful interference in accordance with Articles 28 and 46 respectively, and taking appropriate pre-emptive and remedial measures to that end;\n\n\n(e)promoting the shared use of radio spectrum between similar and/or different uses of spectrum through appropriate established sharing rules and conditions, including the protection of existing rights of use, in accordance with Union law;\n\n\n(f)applying the most appropriate and least onerous authorisation system possible in accordance with Article 46 in such a way as to maximise flexibility, sharing and efficiency in the use of radio spectrum;\n\n\n(g)ensuring that rules for the granting, transfer, renewal, modification and withdrawal of rights to use radio spectrum are clearly and transparently defined and applied in order to guarantee regulatory certainty, consistency and predictability;\n\n\n(h)ensuring consistency and predictability throughout the Union regarding the way the use of radio spectrum is authorised in protecting public health against harmful electromagnetic fields.\n\n\nWhen adopting technical harmonisation measures under Decision No 676/2002/EC, the Commission may, taking utmost account of the opinion of Radio Spectrum Policy Group, adopt an implementing measure setting out whether, pursuant to Article 46 of this Directive, rights in the harmonised band shall be subject to a general authorisation or to individual rights of use. Those implementing measures shall be adopted in accordance with the examination procedure referred to in Article 110(4). \n\n\nWhere the Commission is considering acting to provide for measures in accordance with Article 39, it may seek the advice of the Radio Spectrum Policy Group with regard to the implications of any such standard or specification for the coordination, harmonisation and availability of radio spectrum. The Commission shall take utmost account of the advice of the Radio Spectrum Policy Group in taking any subsequent steps. \n\n\n3. In case of a national or regional lack of market demand for the use of a harmonised band, and subject to the harmonisation measure adopted under Decision No 676/2002/EC, Member States may allow an alternative use of all or part of that band, including the existing use, in accordance with paragraphs 4 and 5, provided that:\n\n\n(a)the finding of a lack of market demand for the use of the harmonised band is based on a public consultation in line with Article 23; \n\n\n(b)such alternative use does not prevent or hinder the availability or the use of the harmonised band  in other Member States; and\n\n\n(c)the Member State concerned takes due account of the long-term availability or use of the harmonised band in the Union and the economies of scale for equipment resulting from using the harmonised radio spectrum in the Union\n\n\nThe alternative use shall only be allowed on an exceptional basis. It shall be subject to a review every three years, or upon request to the competent authority for use of the band in accordance with the harmonisation measure by a prospective user. The Member State shall inform the Commission and the other Member States of the decision taken as well as of the outcome of any review, together with its reasoning.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.10 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n34. Unless otherwise provided in the second subparagraph, Member States shall ensure that all types of technology used for electronic communications services \u00f0\u00a0or networks\u00a0\u00ef may be used in the radio frequency bands\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef , declared available for electronic communications services in their National Frequency Allocation Plan in accordance with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 law.\n\n\n\n\nMember States may, however, provide for proportionate and non-discriminatory restrictions to the types of radio network or wireless access technology used for electronic communications services where this is necessary to:\n\n\n(a) avoid harmful interference;\n\n\n\n(b) protect public health against electromagnetic fields\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0,\u00a0taking utmost account of Council Recommendation No 1999/519/EC\n94\n;\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n(c) ensure technical quality of service;\n\n\n(d) ensure maximisation of radio frequency\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0shared use of radio spectrum resources, in accordance with Union law;\u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n(e) safeguard efficient use of \u00f0\u00a0radio\u00a0\u00ef spectrum; or\n\n\n(f) ensure the fulfilment of a general interest objective in accordance with paragraph\u00a054.\n\n\n45. Unless otherwise provided in the second subparagraph, Member States shall ensure that all types of electronic communications services may be provided in the radio frequency bands\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef , declared available for electronic communications services in their National Frequency Allocation Plan in accordance with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 law. Member States may, however, provide for proportionate and non-discriminatory restrictions to the types of electronic communications services to be provided, including, where necessary, to fulfil a requirement under the ITU Radio Regulations.\n\n\nMeasures that require an electronic communications service to be provided in a specific band available for electronic communications services shall be justified in order to ensure the fulfilment of a general interest objective as defined by Member States in conformity with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 law, such as, and not limited to:\n\n\n(a) safety of life;\n\n\n(b) the promotion of social, regional or territorial cohesion;\n\n\n(c) the avoidance of inefficient use of radio frequencies\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0spectrum\u00a0\u00ef ; or\n\n\n(d) the promotion of cultural and linguistic diversity and media pluralism, for example by the provision of radio and television broadcasting services.\n\n\nA measure which prohibits the provision of any other electronic communications service in a specific band may only be provided for where justified by the need to protect safety of life services. Member States may, exceptionally, also extend such a measure in order to fulfil other general interest objectives as defined by Member States in accordance with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 law.\n\n\n65. Member States shall regularly review the necessity of the restrictions referred to in paragraphs\u00a034 and\u00a045, and shall make the results of these reviews public.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n7. Restrictions established prior to 25 May 2011 shall comply with paragraphs 4 and 5 by the date of application of this Directive .\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.10\n\n\n\n\n6. Paragraphs\u00a03 and\u00a04 shall apply to spectrum allocated to be used for electronic communications services, general authorisations issued and individual rights of use of radio frequencies granted after 25\u00a0May 2011.\n\n\nSpectrum allocations, general authorisations and individual rights of use which existed by 25\u00a0May 2011 shall be subject to Article\u00a09a.\n\n\n7. Without prejudice to the provisions of the Specific Directives and taking into account the relevant national circumstances, Member States may lay down rules in order to prevent spectrum hoarding, in particular by setting out strict deadlines for the effective exploitation of the rights of use by the holder of the rights and by applying penalties, including financial penalties or the withdrawal of the rights of use in case of non-compliance with the deadlines. These rules shall be established and applied in a proportionate, non-discriminatory and transparent manner.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 3.3 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 5\u00a046\u00a0\n\n\nRights of use for radio frequencies and numbers\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Authorisation of the use of radio spectrum\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\n1.
