portability of numbers and other identifiers,\n\n\nany charges due on termination of the contract, including any cost recovery with respect to terminal equipment,(f) any compensation and the refund arrangements which apply if contracted service quality levels are not met;\n\n\n(g) the means of initiating procedures for the settlement of disputes in accordance with Article\u00a034;\n\n\n(h) the type of action that might be taken by the undertaking in reaction to security or integrity incidents or threats and vulnerabilities.\n\n\nMember States may also require that the contract include any information which may be provided by the relevant public authorities for this purpose on the use of electronic communications networks and services to engage in unlawful activities or to disseminate harmful content, and on the means of protection against risks to personal security, privacy and personal data, referred to in Article\u00a021(4) and relevant to the service provided.\n\n\n2. Member States shall ensure that subscribers have a right to withdraw from their contract without penalty upon notice of modification to the contractual conditions proposed by the undertakings providing electronic communications networks and/or services. Subscribers shall be given adequate notice, not shorter than one month, of any such modification, and shall be informed at the same time of their right to withdraw, without penalty, from their contract if they do not accept the new conditions. Member States shall ensure that national regulatory authorities are able to specify the format of such notifications.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a095\n\n\nInformation requirements for contracts\n\n\n1. Before a consumer is bound by a contract or any corresponding offer, providers of publicly available electronic communications services other than number-independent interpersonal communications services, shall provide  the information required pursuant to Articles 5 and 6 of Directive 2011/83/EU, irrespective of the amount of any payment to be made, and the following information in a clear and comprehensible manner:\n\n\n(a) as part of the main characteristics of each service provided:\n\n\n(i) any minimum service quality levels to the extent that these are offered, and in accordance with BEREC guidelines to be adopted after consultation of stakeholders and in close cooperation with the Commission, regarding:\n\n\n\u2013for internet access services: at least latency, jitter, packet loss,\n\n\n\u2013 for publicly available number-based interpersonal communications services: at least the time for the initial connection, failure probability, call signalling delays and\n\n\n\u2013for services other than internet access services within the meaning of Article 3(5) of Regulation 2015/2120: the specific quality parameters assured,\n\n\n(ii) without prejudice to the right of end-users to use terminal equipment of their choice in accordance with Article 3(1) of Regulation 2015/2120/EC, any restrictions imposed by the provider on the use of terminal equipment supplied;\n\n\n(b) any compensation and refund arrangements, which apply if contracted service quality levels are not met;\n\n\n(c) as part of the information on price:\n\n\n(i) details of tariff plans under the contract and, where applicable, the volumes of communications (MB, minutes, SMS) included per billing period, and the price for additional communication units,\n\n\n(ii) tariff information regarding any numbers or services subject to particular pricing conditions; with respect to individual categories of services, NRAs may require such information to be provided immediately prior to connecting the call,   \n\n\n(iii) for bundled services and bundles including both services and equipment the price of the individual elements of the bundle to the extent they are also marketed separately,\n\n\n(iv) details of after-sales service and maintenance charges, and\n\n\n(v) the means by which up-to-date information on all applicable tariffs and maintenance charges may be obtained;\n\n\n(d) as part of the information on the duration of the contract and the conditions for renewal and termination of the contract:\n\n\n(i) any minimum usage or duration required to benefit from promotional terms,\n\n\n(ii) any charges related to switching and the portability of numbers and other identifiers and compensation and refund arrangements for delay or abuse of switching,\n\n\n\n\n(iii) any charges due on early termination of the contract, including any cost recovery with respect to terminal equipment and other promotional advantages,\n\n\n(iv) for bundled services the conditions of termination of the bundle or of elements thereof,\n\n\n(e) details on products and services designed for disabled end-users and how updates on this information can be obtained; \n\n\n(f) the means of initiating procedures for the settlement of disputes in accordance with Article\u00a025;\n\n\n(g) the type of action that might be taken by the undertaking in reaction to security or integrity incidents or threats and vulnerabilities.\n\n\n2. In addition to the requirements set out in paragraph 1 providers of publicly available number-based interpersonal communications services shall provide the following information in a clear and comprehensible manner:\n\n\n\u2013any constraints on access to emergency services and/or caller location information due to a lack of technical feasibility;\n\n\n\u2013the end-user's right to determine whether or not to include his or her personal data in a directory, and the types of data concerned, in accordance with Article 12 of Directive 2002/58/EC;\n\n\n3. Paragraphs 1 and 2 shall apply also to micro or small enterprises as end-users unless they have explicitly agreed to waive all or parts of those provisions,\n\n\n4. Providers of internet access services shall provide the information mentioned in paragraphs\u00a01 and 2 in addition to the information required pursuant to Article 4(1) of Regulation (EU)\u00a02015/2120.\n\n\n5. By [entry into force + 12 months], BEREC shall issue a decision on a contract summary template, which identifies the main elements of the information requirements in accordance with paragraphs 1 and 2. Those main elements shall include at least complete information on:\n\n\n(a)the name and address of the provider,\n\n\n(b)the main characteristics of each service provided,\n\n\n(c)the respective prices, \n\n\n(d)the duration of the contract and the conditions for its renewal and termination,\n\n\n(e)the extent to which the products and services are designed for disabled end-users.\n\n\n(f)with respect to internet access services, the information required pursuant to Article 4\u00a0(1) of Regulation (EU)\u00a02015/2120.\n\n\nProviders subject to the obligations under paragraphs 1-4 shall duly complete this contract summary template with the required information and provide it to consumers, and micro and small enterprises, prior to the conclusion of the contract. The contract summary shall become an integral part of the contract.\n\n\n6. Providers of internet access services and providers of publicly available number-based interpersonal communications services shall offer end-users the facility to monitor and control the usage of each of those services which is billed on the basis of either time or volume consumption. This facility shall include access to timely information on the level of consumption of services included in a tariff plan.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.14\n\n\nArticle\u00a021\n\n\nTransparency and publication of information\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that national regulatory authorities are able to oblige undertakings providing public electronic communications networks and/or publicly available electronic communications services to publish transparent, comparable, adequate and up-to-date information on applicable prices and tariffs, on any charges due on termination of a contract and on standard terms and conditions in respect of access to, and use of, services provided by them to end-users and consumers in accordance with Annex\u00a0II. Such information shall be published in a clear, comprehensive and easily accessible form. National regulatory authorities may specify additional requirements regarding the form in which such information is to be published.\n\n\n2. National regulatory authorities shall encourage the provision of comparable information to enable end-users and consumers to make an independent evaluation of the cost of alternative usage patterns, for instance by means of interactive guides or similar techniques. Where such facilities are not available on the market free of charge or at a reasonable price, Member States shall ensure that national regulatory authorities are able to make such guides or techniques available themselves or through third party procurement. Third parties shall have a right to use, free of charge, the information published by undertakings providing electronic communications networks and/or publicly available electronic communications services for the purposes of selling or making available such interactive guides or similar techniques.\n\n\n3. Member States shall ensure that national regulatory authorities are able to oblige undertakings providing public electronic communications networks and/or publicly available electronic communications services to inter alia:\n\n\n(a) provide applicable tariff information to subscribers regarding any number or service subject to particular pricing conditions; with respect to individual categories of services, national regulatory authorities may require such information to be provided immediately prior to connecting the call;\n\n\n(b) inform subscribers of any change to access to emergency services or caller location information in the service to which they have subscribed;\n\n\n(c) inform subscribers of any change to conditions limiting access to and/or use of services and applications, where such conditions are permitted under national law in accordance with Community law;\n\n\n(d) provide information on any procedures put in place by the provider to measure and shape traffic so as to avoid filling or overfilling a network link, and on how those procedures could impact on service quality;\n\n\n(e) inform subscribers of their right to determine whether or not to include their personal data in a directory, and of the types of data concerned, in accordance with Article\u00a012 of Directive 2002/58/EC (Directive on privacy and electronic communications); and\n\n\n(f) regularly inform disabled subscribers of details of products and services designed for them.\n\n\nIf deemed appropriate, national regulatory authorities may promote self- or co-regulatory measures prior to imposing any obligation.\n\n\n4. Member States may require that the undertakings referred to in paragraph\u00a03 distribute public interest information free of charge to existing and new subscribers, where appropriate, by the same means as those ordinarily used by them in their communications with subscribers. In such a case, that information shall be provided by the relevant public authorities in a standardised format and shall, inter alia, cover the following topics:\n\n\n(a) the most common uses of electronic communications services to engage in unlawful activities or to disseminate harmful content, particularly where it may prejudice respect for the rights and freedoms of others, including infringements of copyright and related rights, and their legal consequences; and\n\n\n(b) the means of protection against risks to personal security, privacy and personal data when using electronic communications services.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a096\n\n\nTransparency, comparison of offers and publication of information\n\n\n\n\n1. National regulatory authorities shall ensure that the information referred to in Annex VIII is published in a clear, comprehensive and easily accessible form by the undertakings providing publicly available electronic communications services other than number-independent interpersonal communications services, or by the national regulatory authority itself. National regulatory authorities may specify additional requirements regarding the form in which such information is to be published.\n\n\n2. National regulatory authorities shall ensure that end-users have access free of charge to at least one independent comparison tool which enables them to compare and evaluate prices and tariffs, and the quality of service performance of different publicly available electronic communcations services other than number-independent interpersonal communications services. \n\n\nThe comparison tool shall:\n\n\n(a)be operationally independent by ensuring that service providers are given equal treatment in search results;\n\n\n(b)clearly disclose their owners and operators;\n\n\n(c)set out clear, objective criteria on which the comparison will be based;\n\n\n(d)use plain and unambiguous language;\n\n\n(e)provide accurate and up-to-date information and state the time of the last update;\n\n\n(f)include a broad range of offers covering a significant part of the market and, where the information presented is not a complete overview of the market, a clear statement to that effect, before displaying results;\n\n\n(g)provide an effective procedure to report incorrect information. \n\n\nComparison tools fulfilling the requirements in points (a) to (g) shall, upon request, be certified by national regulatory authorities. Third parties shall have a right to use, free of charge, the information published by undertakings providing publicly available electronic communications services, other than number-independent interpersonal communications services, for the purposes of making available such independent comparison tools.\n\n\n3. Member States may require that the undertakings providing internet access services or publicly available number-based interpersonal communications services distribute public interest information free of charge to existing and new  end-users, where appropriate, by the same means as those they ordinarily use in their communications with end-users. In such a case, that public interest information shall be provided by the relevant public authorities in a standardised format and shall, inter alia, cover the following topics:\n\n\n(a)the most common uses of internet access services and publicly available number-based interpersonal communications services to engage in unlawful activities or to disseminate harmful content, particularly where it may prejudice respect for the rights and freedoms of others, including infringements of copyright and related rights, and their legal consequences; and\n\n\n(b) the means of protection against risks to personal security, privacy and personal data when using internet access services and publicly available number-based interpersonal communications services.\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.14 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a09722\n\n\nQuality of service\n\n\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that\u00a0nNational regulatory authorities are,\u00a0after taking account of the views of interested parties,\u00a0able to\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0may\u00a0\u00d5 require undertakings that provide\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0providers of\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0 internet access services and of\u00a0\u00ef publicly available electronic\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0number-based interpersonal\u00a0\u00ef communications networks and/or services to publish \u00f0\u00a0comprehensive,\u00a0\u00ef comparable, adequate\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0reliable, user-friendly\u00a0\u00ef and up-to-date information for end-users on the quality of their services and on measures taken to ensure equivalence in access for disabled end-users. That information shall, on request, be supplied to the national regulatory authority in advance of its publication.\n\n\n2. National regulatory authorities may\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0shall\u00a0\u00ef specify, \u00f0\u00a0taking utmost account of BEREC guidelines\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0inter alia, the quality of service parameters to be measured \u00f0\u00a0and the applicable measurement methods,\u00a0\u00ef and the content, form and manner of the information to be published, including possible quality certification mechanisms, in order to ensure that end-users, including disabled end-users, have access to comprehensive, comparable, reliable and user-friendly information. Where appropriate, the parameters, definitions and measurement methods set out in Annex\u00a0III\u00a0IX\u00a0may\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0shall\u00a0\u00ef be used.\n\n\n3. In order to prevent the degradation of service and the hindering or slowing down of traffic over networks, Member States shall ensure that national regulatory authorities are able to set minimum quality of service requirements on an undertaking or undertakings providing public communications networks.\n\n\nNational regulatory authorities shall provide the Commission, in good time before setting any such requirements, with a summary of the grounds for action, the envisaged requirements and the proposed course of action. This information shall also be made available to the Body of European Regulators for Electronic Communications (BEREC). The Commission may, having examined such information, make comments or recommendations thereupon, in particular to ensure that the envisaged requirements do not adversely affect the functioning of the internal market. National regulatory authorities shall take the utmost account of the Commission\u2019s comments or recommendations when deciding on the requirements. \n\n\nBy [entry into force plus 18 months], in order to contribute to a consistent application of this paragraph, BEREC shall adopt, after consultation of stakeholders and in close cooperation with the Commission, guidelines on the relevant quality of service parameters, including parameters relevant for disabled end-users, the applicable measurement methods, the content and format of publication of the information, and quality certification mechanisms.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a098\n\n\nContract duration and termination\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that conditions and procedures for contract termination are not a disincentive against changing service provider and that contracts concluded between consumers and undertakings providing publicly available electronic communications services, other than number-independent interpersonal communications services, do not mandate an initial commitment period longer than 24 months. Member States may adopt or maintain shorter maximum durations for the initial commitment period. \n\n\nThis paragraph shall not apply to the duration of an instalment contract where the consumer has agreed in a separate contract to instalment payments for deployment of a physical connection.\n\n\n2. Where a contract or national law provides for a fixed duration contract to be automatically prolonged, the Member State shall ensure that, after the expiration of the initial period and unless the consumer has explicitly agreed to the extension of the contract, consumers are entitled to terminate the contract at any time with a one-month notice period and without incurring any costs except the cost of providing the service during the notice period.\n\n\n3. End-users shall have the right to terminate their contract without incurring any costs upon notice of changes in the contractual conditions proposed by the provider of publicly available electronic communications services other than number-independent interpersonal communications services, unless the proposed changes are exclusively to the benefit of the end-user or they are strictly necessary to implement legislative or regulatory changes. Providers shall notify end-users, at least one month in advance, of any such change, and shall inform them at the same time of their right to terminate their contract without incurring any costs if they do not accept the new conditions. Member States shall ensure that notification is made in a clear and comprehensible manner on a durable medium and in a format chosen by the end-user at the time of concluding the contract.\n\n\n4. Where an early termination of a contract on a publicly available electronic communications service by the end-user is possible in accordance with this Directive, other provisions of Union law or national law, no compensation shall be due by the end-user other than for the pro rata temporis value of subsidised equipment bundled with the contract at the moment of the contract conclusion and a pro rata temporis reimbursement for any other promotional advantages marked as such at the moment of the contract conclusion. Any restriction on the usage of terminal equipment on other networks shall be lifted, free of charge, by the provider at the latest upon payment of such compensation.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.21 (adapted)\n\n\nArticle\u00a03099\n\n\nFacilitating\u00a0Cchange of provider \u00d6\u00a0and number portability\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0\u00a0\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n1. In case of switching between providers of internet access services, the providers concerned shall provide the end-user with adequate information before and during the switching process and ensure continuity of the service. The receiving provider shall ensure that the activation of the service shall occur on the date agreed with the end-user. The transferring provider shall continue to provide its services on the same terms until the services of the receiving provider are activated. Loss of service during the switching process shall not exceed one working day.\n\n\nNational regulatory authorities shall ensure the efficiency of the switching process for the end-user.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.21\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n12. Member States shall ensure that all subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef with numbers from the national telephone numbering plan who so request can retain their number(s) independently of the undertaking providing the service in accordance with the provisions of Part C of Annex\u00a0IVI.\n\n\n23. National regulatory authorities shall ensure that pricing between operators and/or service providers related to the provision of number portability is cost-oriented, and that \u00f0\u00a0no\u00a0\u00ef direct charges \u00f0\u00a0are applied\u00a0\u00ef to \u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0subscribers if any, do not act as a disincentive for subscribers against changing service provider.\n\n\n34. National regulatory authorities shall not impose retail tariffs for the porting of numbers in a manner that would distort competition, such as by setting specific or common retail tariffs.\n\n\n45. Porting of numbers and their subsequent activation shall be carried out within the shortest possible time. In any case, subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef who have concluded an agreement to port a number to a new undertaking shall have that number activated within one working day \u00f0\u00a0from the conclusion of such an agreement\u00a0\u00ef.\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0The receiving provider shall lead the switching and porting process.\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0Without prejudice to the first subparagraph, competent\u00a0nNational \u00f0\u00a0regulatory\u00a0\u00ef authorities may establish the global process of \u00f0\u00a0switching and of\u00a0\u00ef porting of numbers, taking into account national provisions on contracts, technical feasibility and the need to maintain continuity of service to the subscriber\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-user\u00a0\u00ef. In any event, loss of service during the process of porting shall not exceed one working day. \u00f0\u00a0In case of failure of the porting process, the transferring provider shall reactivate the number of the end-user until the porting is successful\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0Competent\u00a0nNational \u00f0\u00a0regulatory\u00a0\u00ef authorities shall also take into account, where necessary,\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0appropriate\u00a0\u00ef measures ensuring that subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef are \u00f0\u00a0adequately informed and\u00a0\u00ef protected throughout the switching process and are not switched to another provider against their will.\n\n\n56. Member States shall ensure that appropriate sanctions on undertakings are provided for, including an obligation to compensate subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef in case of delay in porting or abuse of porting by them or on their behalf.\n\n\n5. Member States shall ensure that contracts concluded between consumers and undertakings providing electronic communications services do not mandate an initial commitment period that exceeds 24 months. Member States shall also ensure that undertakings offer users the possibility to subscribe to a contract with a maximum duration of 12 months.\n\n\n6. Without prejudice to any minimum contractual period, Member States shall ensure that conditions and procedures for contract termination do not act as a disincentive against changing service provider.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a0100\n\n\nBundled offers\n\n\n1. If a bundle of services or a bundle of services and goods offered to an end-user comprises at least a publicly available electronic communications service other than number-independent interpersonal communications services, Articles 95, 96\u00a0(1), 98 and 99\u00a0(1) shall apply mutatis mutandis to all elements of the bundle except where the provisions applicable to another element of the bundle are more favourable to the end-user. \n\n\n2. Any subscription to additional services or goods provided or distributed by the same provider of publicly available electronic communications services other than number-independent interpersonal communications services  shall not re-start the contract period of the initial contract unless the additional services or goods are offered at a special promotional price available only on the condition that the existing contract period is re-started.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.14\n\n\nArticle\u00a023101\n\n\nAvailability of services\n\n\nMember States shall take all necessary measures to ensure the fullest possible availability of publicly available telephone services provided over public communications networks in the event of catastrophic network breakdown or in cases of force majeure. Member States shall ensure that undertakings providing publicly available telephone services take all necessary measures to ensure uninterrupted access to emergency services.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.17 (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a026102\n\n\nEmergency services\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0communications\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0and the single European emergency call number\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that all end-users of the service referred to in paragraph\u00a02, including users of public pay telephones, are able to call\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0access\u00a0\u00ef the emergency services \u00f0\u00a0through emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef free of charge and without having to use any means of payment, by using the single European emergency call number \u2018112\u2019 and any national emergency call number specified by Member States.\n\n\n2. Member States, in consultation with national regulatory authorities \u00d6\u00a0and\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0, emergency services and providers \u00f0\u00a0of electronic communications services\u00a0\u00ef, shall ensure that undertakings providing end-users with an electronic\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0number-based interpersonal\u00a0\u00ef communications service for originating national calls to a number or numbers in a national telephone numbering plan provide access to emergency services \u00f0\u00a0through emergency communications to the most appropriate PSAP. In case of an appreciable threat to effective access to emergency services the obligation for undertakings may be extended to all interpersonal communications services in accordance with the conditions and procedure set out in Article 59\u00a0(1)\u00a0(c). \u00a0\u00ef\n\n\n3. Member States shall ensure that \u00f0\u00a0all emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0calls to the single European emergency call number \u2018112\u2019 are appropriately answered and handled in the manner best suited to the national organisation of emergency systems. Such calls\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef shall be answered and handled at least as expeditiously and effectively as calls\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef to the national emergency number or numbers, where these continue to be in use. \n\n\n4. Member States shall ensure that access for disabled end-users to emergency services is \u00f0\u00a0available through emergency communications and\u00a0\u00ef equivalent to that enjoyed by other end-users. Measures taken to ensure that disabled end-users are able to access emergency services \u00f0\u00a0through emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef whilst travelling in other Member States shall be based to the greatest extent possible on European standards or specifications published in accordance with the provisions of Article\u00a039\u00a017 of Directive 2002/21/EC (Framework Directive), and they shall not prevent Member States from adopting additional requirements in order to pursue the objectives set out in this Article.\n\n\n5. Member States shall ensure that undertakings concerned make caller location information is \u00f0\u00a0available to the PSAP\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0available free of charge\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0without delay after the emergency communication is set up.\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0to the authority handling emergency calls as soon as the call reaches that authority.\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0Member States shall ensure that the establishment and the transmission of the caller location information are free of charge for the end-user and to the authority handling the emergency communication\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0This shall apply\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0with regard\u00a0\u00d5 to all calls\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef to the single European emergency call number \u2018112\u2019. Member States may extend this\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0that\u00a0\u00d5 obligation to cover calls\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef to national emergency numbers. Competent regulatory authorities shall lay down criteria for the accuracy and reliability of the caller location information provided. \n\n\n6. Member States shall ensure that citizens are adequately informed about the existence and use of the single European emergency call number \u2018112\u2019, in particular through initiatives specifically targeting persons travelling between Member States.\n\n\n7. In order to ensure effective access \u00f0\u00a0to emergency services through emergency communications\u00a0\u00ef to \u2018112\u2019 services in the Member States, the Commission , having consulted BEREC,\u00a0may\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0shall be empowered to\u00a0\u00d5 adopt \u00f0\u00a0delegated acts in accordance with Article 109 on the measures necessary to ensure the compatibility, interoperability, quality, reliability and continuity of emergency communications in the Union with regard to caller location solutions, access for disabled end-users and  routing to the most appropriate PSAP\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0technical implementing measures.\n\n\nHowever, these technical implementing\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Those\u00a0\u00d5 measures shall be adopted without prejudice to, and shall have no impact on, the organisation of emergency services, which remains of\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0in\u00a0\u00d5 the exclusive competence of Member States.\n\n\nThose measures, designed to amend non-essential elements of this Directive by supplementing it, shall be adopted in accordance with the regulatory procedure with scrutiny referred to in Article\u00a037(2).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.15 (adapted)\n\n\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle\u00a023a103\n\n\nEnsuring equivalence in\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Equivalent\u00a0\u00d5 access and choice for disabled end-users\n\n\n1. Member States shall enable\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0ensure that the\u00a0competent  \u00d5\u00a0relevant\u00a0nationalauthorities to specify, where appropriate, requirements to be met by undertakings providing publicly available electronic communications services to ensure that disabled end-users:\n\n\n(a) have access to electronic communications services equivalent to that enjoyed by the majority of end-users; and\n\n\n(b) benefit from the choice of undertakings and services available to the majority of end-users.\n\n\n2. In order to be able to adopt and implement specific arrangements for disabled end-users, Member States shall encourage the availability of terminal equipment offering the necessary services and functions.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\n2. In taking the measures referred to in paragraph\u00a01, Member States shall encourage compliance with the relevant standards or specifications published in accordance with Article 39.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Art.25\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.16(a)\n\n\nArticle 25104\n\n\n\u00e81\u00a0Telephone directory enquiry services\u00a0\u00e7\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.16(b)\n\n\n1. Member States may impose reasonable \u2018must carry\u2019 obligations, for the transmission of specified radio and television broadcast channels and \u00f0\u00a0related\u00a0\u00ef complementary services, particularly accessibility services to enable appropriate access for disabled end-users \u00f0\u00a0and data supporting connected TV services and electronic programme guides\u00a0\u00ef , on undertakings under their jurisdiction providing electronic communications networks used for the distribution of radio or television broadcast channels to the public where a significant number of end-users of such networks use them as their principal means to receive radio and television broadcast channels. Neither paragraph 1 of this Article nor Article 357(2) of Directive 2002/19/EC (Access Directive) shall prejudice the ability of Member States to determine appropriate remuneration, if any, in respect of measures taken in accordance with this Article while ensuring that, in similar circumstances, there is no discrimination in the treatment of undertakings providing electronic communications networks. Where remuneration is provided for, Member States shall ensure that it is applied in a proportionate and transparent manner.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\n\nArticle 29107\n\n\nProvision of additional facilities\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.20(a)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n1. The power to adopt delegated acts is conferred on the Commission subject to the conditions laid down in this Article.\n\n\n2. The delegation of power referred to in Articles 40, 60, 73, 102 and 108 shall be conferred on the Commission for an indeterminate period of time from ... [date of entry into force of the basic legislative act or any other date set by the co-legislators]. \n\n\n3. The delegation of power referred to in Articles 40, 60, 73, 102 and 108 may be revoked at any time by the European Parliament or by the Council. A decision to revoke shall put an end to the delegation of the power specified in that decision. It shall take effect the day following the publication of the decision in the Official Journal of the European Union or at a later date specified therein. It shall not affect the validity of any delegated acts already in force.\n\n\n4. Before adopting a delegated act, the Commission shall consult experts designated by each Member State in accordance with principles laid down in the Interinstitutional Agreement on Better Law-Making of 13 April 2016. \n\n\n5. As soon as it adopts a delegated act, the Commission shall notify it simultaneously to the European Parliament and to the Council.\n\n\n6. A delegated act adopted pursuant to Article(s) 40, 60, 73, 102, and 108  shall enter into force only if no objection has been expressed either by the European Parliament or by the Council within a period of [two months] of notification of that act to the European Parliament and the Council or if, before the expiry of that period, the European Parliament and the Council have both informed the Commission that they will not object. That period shall be extended by [two months] at the initiative of the European Parliament or of the Council.\n\n\nArticle 110\n\n\n\n\nCommittee\n\n\n1. The Commission shall be assisted by a Committee (\u2018the Communications Committee\u2019), established by Directive 2002/21/EC.. That committee shall be a committee within the meaning of Regulation (EU) No 182/2011.\n\n\n2. For the implementing measures referred to in the second subparagraph of Article 45(2), the Committee shall be the Radio Spectrum Committee established pursuant to Article 3(1) of Decision No 676/2002/EC.\n\n\n3. Where reference is made to this paragraph, Article 4 of Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 shall apply.\u00a0Where the opinion of the committee is to be obtained by a written procedure, the procedure shall be terminated without result when, within the time limit for delivery of the opinion, the chair of the committee so decides or a committee member so requests. In such a case, the chair shall convene a committee meeting within a reasonable time.\n\n\n4. Where reference is made to this paragraph, Article\u00a05  of Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 shall apply, having regard to the provisions of Article\u00a08 thereof.\n\n\n5. Where the opinion of the committee is to be obtained by a written procedure, the procedure shall be terminated without result when, within the time limit for delivery of the opinion, the chair of the committee so decides or a committee member so requests. In such a case, the chair shall convene a committee meeting within a reasonable time.\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 23111\n\n\nExchange of information\n\n\n1. The Commission shall provide all relevant information to the Communications Committee on the outcome of regular consultations with the representatives of network operators, service providers, users, consumers, manufacturers and trade unions, as well as third countries and international organisations.\n\n\n2. The Communications Committee shall, taking account of the Community's\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union's\u00a0\u00d5 electronic communications policy, foster the exchange of information between the Member States and between the Member States and the Commission on the situation and the development of regulatory activities regarding electronic communications networks and services.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 24112\n\n\nPublication of information\n\n\n1. Member States shall ensure that up-to-date information pertaining to the application of this Directive and the Specific Directives is made publicly available in a manner that guarantees all interested parties easy access to that information. They shall publish a notice in their national official gazette describing how and where the information is published. The first such notice shall be published before the date of application referred to in Article 11828(1), second subparagraph, and thereafter a notice shall be published whenever there is any change in the information contained therein.\n\n\n2. Member States shall send to the Commission a copy of all such notices at the time of publication. The Commission shall distribute the information to the Communications Committee as appropriate.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 3.9\n\n\n13. Member States shall ensure that all relevant information on rights, conditions, procedures, charges, fees and decisions concerning general authorisations, rights of use and rights to install facilities is published and kept up to date in an appropriate manner so as to provide easy access to that information for all interested parties.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC\n\n\n24. Where information as referred to in paragraph 13 is held at different levels of government, in particular information regarding procedures and conditions on rights to install facilities, the national regulatory authority shall make all reasonable efforts, bearing in mind the costs involved, to create a user-friendly overview of all such information, including information on the relevant levels of government and the responsible authorities, in order to facilitate applications for rights to install facilities.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\n\n15. Member States shall ensure that the specific obligations imposed on undertakings under this Directive are published and that the specific product/service and geographical markets are identified. They shall ensure that up-to-date information, provided that the information is not confidential and, in particular, does not comprise business secrets, is made publicly available in a manner that guarantees all interested parties easy access to that information.\n\n\n26. Member States shall send to the Commission a copy of all such information published. The Commission shall make this information available in a readily accessible form, and shall distribute the information to the Communications Committee as appropriate.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\n\nArticle 36113\n\n\nNotification and monitoring\n\n\n1. National regulatory authorities shall notify to the Commission by at the latest the date of application referred to in Article 11838(1), second subparagraph, and immediately in the event of any change thereafter in the names of undertakings designated as having universal service obligations under Articles\u00a08(1)\u00a084(1) or 85.\n\n\nThe Commission shall make the information available in a readily accessible form, and shall distribute it to the Communications Committee referred to in Article 11137.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.26\n\n\n2. National regulatory authorities shall notify to the Commission the universal service obligations imposed upon undertakings designated as having universal service obligations. Any changes affecting these obligations or of the undertakings affected under the provisions of this Directive shall be notified to the Commission without delay.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\n\n\n\n3. The Commission shall periodically review the functioning of this Directive and report to the European Parliament and to the Council, on the first occasion not later than three years after the date of application referred to in Article 38(1), second subparagraph. The Member States and national regulatory authorities shall supply the necessary information to the Commission for this purpose.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Art.16\n\n\n1. Member States shall notify to the Commission by at the latest the date of application referred to in Article 18(1) second subparagraph the national regulatory authorities responsible for the tasks set out in this Directive.\n\n\n24. National regulatory authorities shall notify to the Commission the names of operators deemed to have significant market power for the purposes of this Directive, and the obligations imposed upon them under this Directive. Any changes affecting the obligations imposed upon undertakings or of the undertakings affected under the provisions of this Directive shall be notified to the Commission without delay.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nArticle 25114\n\n\nReview procedures\n\n\n1. The Commission shall periodically review the functioning of this Directive and report to the European Parliament and to the Council, on the first occasion not later than three\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0five\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0 years after the date of application referred to in Article115\u00a028(1), second subparagraph. For this purpose, the Commission may request information from the Member States, which shall be supplied without undue delay.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\n\n2. The Commission shall periodically review the functioning of this Directive and report to the European Parliament and to the Council, on the first occasion not later than three years after the date of application referred to in Article 18(1), second subparagraph. For this purpose, the Commission may request from the Member States information, which shall be supplied without undue delay.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC\n\n\n3. The Commission shall periodically review the functioning of the national authorisation systems and the development of cross-border service provision within the Community and report to the European Parliament and to the Council on the first occasion not later than three years after the date of application of this Directive referred to in Article 18(1), second subparagraph. For this purpose, the Commission may request from the Member States information, which shall be supplied without undue delay.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC Art. 15   (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\n\n12. The Commission shall periodically review the scope of universal service, in particular with a view to proposing to the European Parliament and the Council that the scope be changed or redefined. A review shall be carried out, on the first occasion within two years after the date of application referred to in Article 38(1), second subparagraph, and subsequently every three\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0five\u00a0\u00ef years.\n\n\n23. This review shall be undertaken in the light of social, economic and technological developments, taking into account, inter alia, mobility and data rates in the light of the prevailing technologies used by the majority of subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef . The review process shall be undertaken in accordance with Annex V. The Commission shall submit a report to the European Parliament and the Council regarding the outcome of the review.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 26\n\n\nRepeal\n\n\nThe following Directives and Decisions are hereby repealed with effect from the date of application referred to in Article 28(1), second subparagraph:\n\n\n\u2013Directive 90/387/EEC,\n\n\n\u2013Council Decision 91/396/EEC of 29 July 1991 on the introduction of a single European emergency call number\n104\n,\n\n\n\u2013Council Directive 92/44/EEC of 5 June 1992 on the application of open network provision to leased lines\n105\n,\n\n\n\u2013Council Decision 92/264/EEC of 11 May 1992 on the introduction of a standard international telephone access code in the Community\n106\n,\n\n\n\u2013Directive 95/47/EC,\n\n\n\u2013Directive 97/13/EC,\n\n\n\u2013Directive 97/33/EC,\n\n\n\u2013Directive 98/10/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 26 February 1998 on the application of open network provision (ONP) to voice telephony and on universal service for telecommunications in a competitive environment\n107\n.\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 1.26\n\n\n\n\u2013\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\n\n\nArticle 28\n\n\nTransposition\n\n\n1. Member States shall adopt and publish the laws, regulations and administrative provisions necessary to comply with this Directive not later than 24 July 2003. They shall forthwith inform the Commission thereof.\n\n\nThey shall apply those measures from 25 July 2003.\n\n\n2. When Member States adopt these measures, they shall contain a reference to this Directive or be accompanied by such a reference on the occasion of their official publication. The methods of making such a reference shall be laid down by the Member States.\n\n\n3. Member States shall communicate to the Commission the text of the provisions of national law which they adopt in the field governed by this Directive and of any subsequent amendments to those provisions.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 18\n\n\nTransposition\n\n\n1. Member States shall adopt and publish the laws, regulations and administrative provisions necessary to comply with this Directive by 24 July 2003 at the latest. They shall forthwith inform the Commission thereof.\n\n\nThey shall apply those measures from 25 July 2003.\n\n\nWhen Member States adopt these measures, they shall contain a reference to this Directive or be accompanied by such reference on the occasion of their official publication. The methods of making such reference shall be laid down by Member States.\n\n\n2. Member States shall communicate to the Commission the text of the provisions of national law which they adopt in the field governed by this Directive and of any subsequent amendments to those provisions.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 18\n\n\nTransposition\n\n\n1. Member States shall adopt and publish the laws, regulations and administrative provisions necessary to comply with this Directive by not later than 24 July 2003. They shall forthwith inform the Commission thereof.\n\n\nThey shall apply those measures from 25 July 2003.\n\n\n\n\nWhen Member States adopt these measures, they shall contain a reference to this Directive or be accompanied by such a reference on the occasion of their official publication. The methods of making such reference shall be laid down by Member States.\n\n\n2. Member States shall communicate to the Commission the text of the provisions of national law which they adopt in the field governed by this Directive and of any subsequent amendments to those provisions.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 38\n\n\nTransposition\n\n\n1. Member States shall adopt and publish the laws, regulations and administrative provisions necessary to comply with this Directive by 24 July 2003 at the latest. They shall forthwith inform the Commission thereof.\u00a0They shall apply those measures from 25 July 2003.\n\n\n2. When Member States adopt these measures, they shall contain a reference to this Directive or be accompanied by such a reference on the occasion of their official publication. The methods of making such a reference shall be laid down by the Member States.\n\n\n3. Member States shall communicate to the Commission the text of the provisions of national law which they adopt in the field governed by this Directive and of any subsequent modifications to those provisions.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 19\n\n\nEntry into force\n\n\nThis Directive shall enter into force on the day of its publication in the Official Journal of the European Communities.\n\n\nArticle 20\n\n\nAddressees\n\n\nThis Directive is addressed to the Member States.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/20/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 19\n\n\n\n\nEntry into force\n\n\nThis Directive shall enter into force on the day of its publication in the Official Journal of the European Communities.\n\n\nArticle 20\n\n\nAddressees\n\n\nThis Directive is addressed to the Member States.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/21/EC (adapted)\n\n\nArticle 29\n\n\nEntry into force\n\n\nThis Directive shall enter into force on the day of its publication in the Official Journal of the European Communities.\n\n\nArticle 30\n\n\nAddressees\n\n\nThis Directive is addressed to the Member States.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC\n\n\n\nArticle 39\n\n\nEntry into force\n\n\nThis Directive shall enter into force on the day of its publication in the Official Journal of the European Communities.\n\n\nArticle 40\n\n\n\n\nAddressees\n\n\nThis Directive is addressed to the Member States.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a0\n\n\nArticle 115\n\n\nTransposition\n\n\n1.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Member States shall adopt and publish, by\u00a0[day/month/year], the laws, regulations and administrative provisions necessary to comply with Articles [ \u2026] and Annexes [\u2026].\u00a0They shall immediately communicate the text of those measures to the Commission.\n\n\nThey shall apply those measures from [day/month/year].\n\n\nWhen Member States adopt those measures, they shall contain a reference to this Directive or be accompanied by such a reference on the occasion of their official publication. They shall also include a statement that references in existing laws, regulations and administrative provisions to the Directives repealed by this Directive shall be construed as references to this Directive. Member States shall determine how such reference is to be made and how that statement is to be formulated.\n\n\n2.\n\u00a0\u00a0\u00a0Member States shall communicate to the Commission the text of the main provisions of national law which they adopt in the field covered by this Directive.\n\n\nArticle 116\n\n\nRepeal\n\n\nDirectives 2002/19/EC, 2002/20/EC, 2002/21/EC, 2002/22/EC  ,listed in Annex XI, Part A, are repealed with effect from [\u2026], without prejudice to the obligations of the Member States relating to the timelimits for the transposition into national law and the dates of application of the Directives set out in Annex XI, Part B.\n\n\nReferences to the repealed Directives shall be construed as references to this Directive and shall be read in accordance with the correlation table in Annex XII.\n\n\nArticle 117\n\n\nEntry into force\n\n\nThis Directive shall enter into force on on the twentieth day following that of its publication in the Official Journal of code.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC (adapted)\n\n\n\nANNEX II\n\n\nCONDITIONS FOR ACCESS TO DIGITAL TELEVISION AND RADIO SERVICES BROADCAST TO VIEWERS AND LISTENERS IN THE COMMUNITY\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0UNION\u00a0\u00d5\n\n\nPart I: Conditions for conditional access systems to be applied in accordance with Article 660(1)\n\n\nIn relation to conditional access to digital television and radio services broadcast to viewers and listeners in the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 , irrespective of the means of transmission, Member States must ensure in accordance with Article 6\u00a060 that the following conditions apply:\n\n\n(a) conditional access systems operated on the market in the Community are to have the necessary technical capability for cost-effective transcontrol allowing the possibility for full control by network operators at local or regional level of the services using such conditional access systems;\n\n\n(ba) all operators of conditional access services, irrespective of the means of transmission, who provide access services to digital television and radio services and whose access services broadcasters depend on to reach any group of potential viewers or listeners are to:\n\n\n\u2013offer to all broadcasters, on a fair, reasonable and non-discriminatory basis compatible with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 competition law, technical services enabling the broadcasters' digitally-transmitted services to be received by viewers or listeners authorised by means of decoders administered by the service operators, and comply with Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 competition law,\n\n\n\u2013keep separate financial accounts regarding their activity as conditional access providers.\n\n\n(cb) when granting licences to manufacturers of consumer equipment, holders of industrial property rights to conditional access products and systems are to ensure that this is done on fair, reasonable and non-discriminatory terms. Taking into account technical and commercial factors, holders of rights are not to subject the granting of licences to conditions prohibiting, deterring or discouraging the inclusion in the same product of:\n\n\n\u2013a common interface allowing connection with several other access systems, or\n\n\n\u2013means specific to another access system, provided that the licensee complies with the relevant and reasonable conditions ensuring, as far as he is concerned, the security of transactions of conditional access system operators.\n\n\nPart II: Other facilities to which conditions may be applied under Article 559(1)(b)\n\n\n(a) Access to application program interfaces (APIs);\n\n\n\n\n(b) Access to electronic programme guides (EPGs).\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 2.12(a)\n\n\nANNEX II\n\n\nMINIMUM LIST OF ITEMS TO BE INCLUDED IN A REFERENCE OFFER FOR WHOLESALE NETWORK INFRASTRUCTURE ACCESS, INCLUDING SHARED OR FULLY UNBUNDLED ACCESS TO THE LOCAL LOOP AT A FIXED LOCATION TO BE PUBLISHED BY NOTIFIED OPERATORS WITH SIGNIFICANT MARKET POWER (SMP)\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\n\nFor the purposes of this Annex the following definitions apply:\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 2.12(b)\n\n\n(a)\u2018local sub-loop\u2019 means a partial local loop connecting the network termination point to a concentration point or a specified intermediate access point in the fixed public electronic communications network;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\n\n(b)\u2018unbundled access to the local loop\u2019 means full unbundled access to the local loop and shared access to the local loop; it does not entail a change in ownership of the local loop;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 2.12(c)\n\n\n(c)\u2018full unbundled access to the local loop\u2019 means the provision to a beneficiary of access to the local loop or local sub-loop of the SMP operator allowing the use of the full capacity of the network infrastructure;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 2.12(d)\n\n\n(d)\u2018shared access to the local loop\u2019 means the provision to a beneficiary of access to the local loop or local sub-loop of the SMP operator, allowing the use of a specified part of the capacity of the network infrastructure such as a part of the frequency or an equivalent.\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\n\nA.Conditions for unbundled access to the local loop\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 2.12(e)\n\n\n1. Network elements to which access is offered covering in particular the following elements together with appropriate associated facilities:\n\n\n(a) unbundled access to local loops (full and shared);\n\n\n(b) unbundled access to local sub-loops (full and shared), including, when relevant, access to network elements which are not active for the purpose of roll-out of backhaul networks;\n\n\n(c) where relevant, duct access enabling the roll out of access networks.\n\n\n2. Information concerning the locations of physical access sites including cabinets and distribution frames, availability of local loops, sub-loops and backhaul in specific parts of the access network and when relevant, information concerning the locations of ducts and the availability within ducts;\n\n\n3. Technical conditions related to access and use of local loops and sub-loops, including the technical characteristics of the twisted pair and/or optical fibre and/or equivalent, cable distributors, and associated facilities and, when relevant, technical conditions related to access to ducts;\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\n\n4. Ordering and provisioning procedures, usage restrictions.\n\n\nB.Co-location services\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/140/EC Art. 2.12(f)\n\n\n1. Information on the SMP operator's existing relevant sites or equipment locations and planned update thereof\n7\n.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/19/EC\n\n\n\n\n2. Co-location options at the sites indicated under point 1 (including physical co-location and, as appropriate, distant co-location and virtual co-location).\n\n\n3. Equipment characteristics: restrictions, if any, on equipment that can be co-located.\n\n\n4. Security issues: measures put in place by notified operators to ensure the security of their locations.\n\n\n5. Access conditions for staff of competitive operators.\n\n\n6. Safety standards.\n\n\n7. Rules for the allocation of space where co-location space is limited.\n\n\n8. Conditions for beneficiaries to inspect the locations at which physical co-location is available, or sites where co-location has been refused on grounds of lack of capacity.\n\n\nC.Information systems\n\n\nConditions for access to notified operator's operational support systems, information systems or databases for pre-ordering, provisioning, ordering, maintenance and repair requests and billing.\n\n\nD.Supply conditions\n\n\n1. Lead time for responding to requests for supply of services and facilities; service level agreements, fault resolution, procedures to return to a normal level of service and quality of service parameters.\n\n\n2. Standard contract terms, including, where appropriate, compensation provided for failure to meet lead times.\n\n\n3. Prices or pricing formulae for each feature, function and facility listed above.\n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nANNEX III\n\n\nCriteria for the determination of wholesale call termination rates \n\n\n\nCriteria and parameters for the determination of rates for wholesale call termination on fixed and mobile markets, referred to in Article 73 (4):\n\n\n\n\n\n(a)the relevant incremental costs of the wholesale voice call termination service shall be determined by the difference between the total long-run costs of an operator providing its full range of services and the total long-run costs of that operator not providing a wholesale voice call termination service to third parties;\n\n\n(b)only those traffic related costs which would be avoided in the absence of a wholesale voice call termination service being provided shall be allocated to the relevant termination increment;\n\n\n(c)costs related to additional network capacity shall be included only to the extent that they are driven by the need to increase capacity for the purpose of carrying additional wholesale voice call termination traffic;\n\n\n(d)radio spectrum fees shall be excluded from the mobile termination increment;\n\n\n(e)only those wholesale commercial costs shall be included which are directly related to the provision of the wholesale voice call termination service to third parties;\n\n\n(f)all fixed network operators shall be deemed to provide voice call termination services at the same unit costs as the efficient operator, regardless of their size;\n\n\n(g)for mobile network operators, the minimum efficient scale shall be set at a market share not below 20%;\n\n\n(h)the relevant approach for asset depreciation shall be economic depreciation; and\n\n\n(i)the technology choice of the modelled networks shall be forward looking, based on an IP core network, taking into account the various technologies likely to be used over the period of validity of the maximum rate. In the case of fixed networks, calls shall be considered to be exclusively packet switched.\n\n\nANNEX IV\n\n\nCRITERIA FOR ASSESSING CO-INVESTMENT OFFERS\n\n\nWhen assessing a co-investment offer pursuant to Article 74 (1) (d), the national regulatory authority shall verify whether the following criteria have been met: \n\n\n(a)The co-investment offer shall be open to any undertaking over the lifetime of the network built under a co-investment offer on a non-discriminatory basis. The SMP operator may include in the offer reasonable conditions regarding the financial capacity of any undertaking, so that for instance potential co-investors need to demonstrate their ability to deliver phased payments on the basis of which the deployment is planned, the acceptance of a strategic plan on the basis of which medium-term deployment plans are prepared, etc. \n\n\n(b)The co-investment offer shall be transparent:\n\n\n\u2013the offer is available and easily identified on the website of the SMP operator;\n\n\n\u2013full detailed terms must be made available without undue delay to any potential bidder that has expressed an interest, including  the legal form of the co-investment agreement and -  when relevant - the heads of term of the governance rules of the co-investment vehicle; and\n\n\n\u2013The process, like the road map for the establishment and development of the co-investment project must be set in advance, it must clearly explained in writing to any potential co-investor, and all significant milestones be clearly communicated to all undertakings without any discrimination. \n\n\n(c)The co-investment offer shall include terms to potential co-investors which favour sustainable competition in the long term, in particular: \n\n\n\u2013All undertakings have to be offered fair, reasonable and non-discriminatory terms and conditions for participation in the co-investment agreement relative to the time they join, including in terms of financial consideration required for the acquisition of specific rights, in terms of the protection awarded to the co-investors by those rights both during the building phase and during the exploitation phase, for example by granting indefeasible rights of use (IRUs) for the expected lifetime of the co-invested network and in terms of the conditions for joining and potentially terminating the co-investment agreement. Non-discriminatory terms in this context do not entail that all potential co-investors must be offered exactly the same terms, including financial terms, but that all variations of the terms offered must be justified on the basis of the same objective, transparent, non-discriminatory and predictable criteria such as the number of end user lines committed for.\n\n\n\u2013The offer must allow flexibility in terms of the value and timing of the commitment provided by each co-investor, for example by means of an agreed and potentially increasing percentage of the total end user lines in a given area, to which co-investors have the possibility to commit gradually and which shall be set at a unit level enabling smaller co-investors to gradually increase their participation while ensuring adequate levels of initial commitment. The determination of the financial consideration to be provided by each co-investor needs to reflect the fact that early investors accept greater risks and engage capital sooner.\n\n\n\n\n\u2013A premium increasing over time has to be considered as justified for commitments made at later stages and for new co-investors entering the co-investment after the commencement of the project, to reflect diminishing risks and to counteract any incentive to withhold capital in the earlier stages. \n\n\n\u2013The co-investment agreement has to allow the assignment of acquired rights by co-investors to other co-investors, or to third parties willing to enter into the co-investment agreement subject to the transferee undertaking being obliged to fulfil all original obligations of the transferor under the co-investment agreement.\n\n\n\u2013Co-investors have to grant each other reciprocal rights on fair and reasonable terms and conditions to access the co-invested infrastructure for the purposes of providing services downstream, including to end-users, according to transparent conditions which have to be made transparent in the co-investment offer and subsequent agreement, in particular where co-investors are individually and separately responsible for the deployment of specific parts of the network. If a co-investment vehicle is created, it has to provide access to the network to all co-investors, whether directly or indirectly, on an equivalence of inputs basis and according to fair and reasonable terms and conditions, including financial conditions that reflect the different levels of risk accepted by the individual co-investors. \n\n\n(d)The co-investment offer shall ensure a sustainable investment likely to meet future needs, by deploying new network elements that contribute significantly to the deployment of very high capacity networks. \n\n\n\n\u00f2\u00a0new\n\n\nANNEX of all type of information \n\n\n(3)basic training and education online tools\n\n\n(4)online newspapers/news\n\n\n(5)buying/ordering goods or services online\n\n\n(6)job searching and job searching tools\n\n\n(7)professional networking\n\n\n(8)internet banking\n\n\n(9)eGovernment service use\n\n\n(10)social media and instant messaging\n\n\n(11)calls and video calls (standard quality)\n\n\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.28 and Annex I (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\nANNEX\u00a0IVI\n\n\nDESCRIPTION OF FACILITIES AND SERVICES REFERRED TO IN ARTICLE\u00a010\u00a083 (CONTROL OF EXPENDITURE), ARTICLE\u00a029\u00a0107 (ADDITIONAL FACILITIES) AND ARTICLE\u00a030\u00a099 (FACILITATING CHANGE OF PROVIDER \u00d6\u00a0AND NUMBER PORTABILITY\u00a0\u00d5 )\n\n\nPart A: Facilities and services referred to in Article\u00a01083\n\n\n(a) Itemised billing\n\n\nMember States are to ensure that national regulatory authorities, subject to the requirements of relevant legislation on the protection of personal data and privacy, may lay down the basic level of itemised bills which are to be provided by undertakings to subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef free of charge in order that they can:\n\n\n(i) allow verification and control of the charges incurred in using the public communications network at a fixed location and/or related publicly available telephone\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0voice communications\u00a0\u00ef services \u00f0\u00a0, or number-based interpersonal communications services in the case of Article 107\u00a0\u00ef ; and\n\n\n(ii) adequately monitor their usage and expenditure and thereby exercise a reasonable degree of control over their bills.\n\n\nWhere appropriate, additional levels of detail may be offered to subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef at reasonable tariffs or at no charge.\n\n\nCalls which are free of charge to the calling subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef, including calls to helplines, are not to be identified in the calling subscriber's\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end user's\u00a0\u00ef itemised bill.\n\n\n(b) Selective barring for outgoing calls or premium SMS or MMS, or, where technically feasible, other kinds of similar applications, free of charge\n\n\ni.e. the facility whereby the subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef can, on request to the designated undertaking that provides telephone\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0voice communications\u00a0\u00ef services \u00f0\u00a0, or number-based interpersonal communications services in the case of Article 107\u00a0\u00ef , bar outgoing calls or premium SMS or MMS or other kinds of similar applications of defined types or to defined types of numbers free of charge.\n\n\n(c) Pre-payment systems\n\n\nMember States are to ensure that national regulatory authorities may require designated undertakings to provide means for consumers to pay for access to the public communications network and use of publicly available telephone\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0voice communications\u00a0\u00ef services \u00f0\u00a0, or number-based interpersonal communications services in the case of Article 107,\u00a0\u00ef on pre-paid terms.\n\n\n(d) Phased payment of connection fees\n\n\nMember States are to ensure that national regulatory authorities may require designated undertakings to allow consumers to pay for connection to the public communications network on the basis of payments phased over time.\n\n\n(e) Non-payment of bills\n\n\nMember States are to authorise specified measures, which are to be proportionate, non-discriminatory and published, to cover non-payment of telephone bills issued by undertakings. These measures are to ensure that due warning of any consequent service interruption or disconnection is given to the subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef beforehand. Except in cases of fraud, persistent late payment or non-payment, these measures are to ensure, as far as is technically feasible that any service interruption is confined to the service concerned. Disconnection for non-payment of bills should take place only after due warning is given to the subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef . Member States may allow a period of limited service prior to complete disconnection, during which only calls that do not incur a charge to the subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef (e.g. \u2018112\u2019 calls) are permitted.\n\n\n(f) Tariff advice\n\n\n\n\ni.e. the facility whereby subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef may request the undertaking to provide information regarding alternative lower-cost tariffs, if available.\n\n\n(g) Cost control\n\n\ni.e. the facility whereby undertakings offer other means, if determined to be appropriate by national regulatory authorities, to control the costs of publicly available telephone\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0voice communications\u00a0\u00ef services, \u00f0\u00a0or number-based interpersonal communications services in the case of Article 107,\u00a0\u00ef including free-of-charge alerts to consumers in case of abnormal or excessive consumption patterns.\n\n\nPart B: Facilities referred to in Article\u00a029107\n\n\n(a) Tone dialling or DTMF (dual-tone multi-frequency operation)\n\n\ni.e. the public communications network and/or publicly available telephone services supports the use of DTMF tones as defined in ETSI ETR 207 for end-to-end signalling throughout the network both within a Member State and between Member States.\n\n\n(b) Calling-line identification\n\n\ni.e. the calling party\u2019s number is presented to the called party prior to the call being established.\n\n\nThis facility should be provided in accordance with relevant legislation on protection of personal data and privacy, in particular Directive 2002/58/EC (Directive on privacy and electronic communications).\n\n\nTo the extent technically feasible, operators should provide data and signals to facilitate the offering of calling-line identity and tone dialling across Member State boundaries.\n\n\nPart C: Implementation of the number portability provisions referred to in Article\u00a03099\n\n\nThe requirement that all subscribers\u00a0\u00f0\u00a0end-users\u00a0\u00ef with numbers from the national numbering plan, who so request can retain their number(s) independently of the undertaking providing the service shall apply:\n\n\n(a) in the case of geographic numbers, at a specific location; and\n\n\n(b) in the case of non-geographic numbers, at any location.\n\n\nThis Part does not apply to the porting of numbers between networks providing services at a fixed location and mobile networks.\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02002/22/EC (adapted)\n\n\n\u00f0\u00a0new\n\n\n\nANNEX IVVII\n\n\n\n\nCALCULATING THE NET COST, IF ANY, OF UNIVERSAL SERVICE OBLIGATIONS AND ESTABLISHING ANY RECOVERY OR SHARING MECHANISM IN ACCORDANCE WITH ARTICLES 12\u00a084 AND 1385\n\n\nPart A: Calculation of net cost\n\n\nUniversal service obligations refer to those obligations placed upon an undertaking by a Member State which concern the provision of \u00f0\u00a0universal service as set out in Articles 79, 81 and 82\u00a0\u00ef\u00a0a network and service throughout a specified geographical area, including, where required, averaged prices in that geographical area for the provision of that service or provision of specific tariff options for consumers with low incomes or with special social needs.\n\n\nNational regulatory authorities are to consider all means to ensure appropriate incentives for undertakings (designated or not) to provide universal service obligations cost efficiently. In undertaking a calculation exercise, the net cost of universal service obligations is to be calculated as the difference between the net cost for \u00d6\u00a0any\u00a0\u00d5\u00a0designated undertaking of operating with the universal service obligations and operating without the universal service obligations. This applies whether the network in a particular Member State is fully developed or is still undergoing development and expansion. Due attention is to be given to correctly assessing the costs that any designated undertaking would have chosen to avoid had there been no universal service obligation. The net cost calculation should assess the benefits, including intangible benefits, to the universal service operator.\n\n\nThe calculation is to be based upon the costs attributable to:\n\n\n(i) elements of the identified services which can only be provided at a loss or provided under cost conditions falling outside normal commercial standards.\n\n\nThis category may include service elements such as access to emergency telephone services, provision of certain public pay telephones, provision of certain services or equipment for disabled people, etc;\n\n\n(ii) specific end-users or groups of end-users who, taking into account the cost of providing the specified network and service, the revenue generated and any geographical averaging of prices imposed by the Member State, can only be served at a loss or under cost conditions falling outside normal commercial standards.\n\n\nThis category includes those end-users or groups of end-users which would not be served by a commercial operator which did not have an obligation to provide universal service.\n\n\nThe calculation of the net cost of specific aspects of universal service obligations is to be made separately and so as to avoid the double counting of any direct or indirect benefits and costs. The overall net cost of universal service obligations to any undertaking is to be calculated as the sum of the net costs arising from the specific components of universal service obligations, taking account of any intangible benefits. The responsibility for verifying the net cost lies with the national regulatory authority.\n\n\nPart B: Recovery of any net costs of universal service obligations\n\n\nThe recovery or financing of any net costs of universal service obligations requires designated undertakings with universal service obligations to be compensated for the services they provide under non-commercial conditions. Because such a compensation involves financial transfers, Member States are to ensure that these are undertaken in an objective, transparent, non-discriminatory and proportionate manner. This means that the transfers result in the least distortion to competition and to user demand.\n\n\nIn accordance with Article 13(3), a sharing mechanism based on a fund should use a transparent and neutral means for collecting contributions that avoids the danger of a double imposition of contributions falling on both outputs and inputs of undertakings.\n\n\nThe independent body administering the fund is to be responsible for collecting contributions from undertakings which are assessed as liable to contribute to the net cost of universal service obligations in the Member State and is to oversee the transfer of sums due and/or administrative payments to the undertakings entitled to receive payments from the fund.\n\n\nANNEX\u00a0IIVIII\n\n\nINFORMATION TO BE PUBLISHED IN ACCORDANCE WITH ARTICLE\u00a02196\n\n\n(TRANSPARENCY AND PUBLICATION OF INFORMATION)\n\n\nThe national regulatory authority has a responsibility to ensure that the information in this Annex is published, in accordance with Article\u00a02196. universal service obligations should be undertaken, the Commission is to take into consideration the following elements:\n\n\n\n\n\u2013social and market developments in terms of the services used by consumers,\n\n\n\u2013social and market developments in terms of the availability and choice of services to consumers,\n\n\n\u2013technological developments in terms of the way services are provided to consumers.\n\n\nIn considering whether the scope of universal service obligations be changed or redefined, the Commission is to take into consideration the following elements:\n\n\n\u2013are specific services available to and used by a majority of consumers and does the lack of availability or non-use by a minority of consumers result in social exclusion, and\n\n\n\u2013does the availability and use of specific services convey a general net benefit to all consumers such that public intervention is warranted in circumstances where the specific services are not provided to the public under normal commercial circumstances?\n\n\n\n\u00ea\u00a02009/136/EC Art. 1.28 and Annex II (adapted)\n\n\nANNEX\u00a0VI\u00a0X\n\n\nINTEROPERABILITY OF DIGITAL CONSUMER EQUIPMENT REFERRED TO IN ARTICLE\u00a024105\n\n\n1. Common scrambling algorithm and free-to-air reception\n\n\nAll consumer equipment intended for the reception of conventional digital television signals (i.e. broadcasting via terrestrial, cable or satellite transmission which is primarily intended for fixed reception, such as DVB-T, DVB-C or DVB-S), for sale or rent or otherwise made available in the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 , capable of descrambling digital television signals, is to possess the capability to:\n\n\n\u2013allow the descrambling of such signals according to a common European scrambling algorithm as administered by a recognised European standards organisation, currently ETSI,\n\n\n\u2013display signals that have been transmitted in the clear provided that, in the event that such equipment is rented, the renter is in compliance with the relevant rental agreement.\n\n\n2. Interoperability for analogue and digital television sets\n\n\nAny analogue television set with an integral screen of visible diagonal greater than 42\u00a0cm which is put on the market for sale or rent in the Community is to be fitted with at least one open interface socket, as standardised by a recognised European standards organisation, e.g. as given in the Cenelec EN 50\u00a0049-1:1997 standard, permitting simple connection of peripherals, especially additional decoders and digital receivers.\n\n\nAny digital television set with an integral screen of visible diagonal greater than 30\u00a0cm which is put on the market for sale or rent in the Community\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0Union\u00a0\u00d5 is to be fitted with at least one open interface socket (either standardised by, or conforming to a standard adopted by, a recognised European standards organisation, or conforming to an industry-wide specification) e.g. the DVB common interface connector, permitting simple connection of peripherals, and able to pass all the\u00a0\u00d6\u00a0relevant\u00a0\u00d5 elements of a digital television signal, including information relating to interactive and conditionally
